de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the carnositis called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you apply the cautery to althelul (possibly an herb), heat the cautery which seems like a razor, and then place it all around the althelul, covering it; leave your hand there so that the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, causing it to close; do this once or twice, and if there is much althelul, cauterize each one as we have said; after that, heal with ointments until they are healthy; and if you cauterize a large cautery on alchatim (possibly a lesion), it will have more aid.
de plaie mal curee	of an improperly healed wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	If the patient cannot bear any incision or opening, as we will explain in its place, this disease comes that can only be cured by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. de la routure dou syfac	Of the rupture of the siphon

tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor. s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence .i. autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	When pain comes in any member, either due to falling or injury, and this pain lasts for a long time, and the medicine cures do not work; then it should be cauterized with the cautery called "poins", and the cauteries should be according to the length of the limb and its smallness and weakness and its virtue and its location of twisting and of its pain. If the patient is healed by the first cautery, that's good; if not, repeat another cautery on top of it, because it is customary that the member should change with the cauteries; therefore, you should perform the cauteries as many times as the patient is healed.
de meselerie	In mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie. The medicines are sometimes helped by cauterization with great assistance, and the same applies to diseases that come from putrefaction of fleume (fever) and melancholy. If you see the patient being cauterized at the beginning, take care and ensure that it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and do not doubt that the corruption will affect the entire patient; then you should apply five cauteries on the head: one on the forehead towards the end of the hair, two on both horns, and one behind the neck; and leave your hand enough so that the cautery reaches the bone, and enough that the bark comes out from it, allowing the vapors of gross humors to escape; then cauterize the wound according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixture is scattered everywhere; it clearly perishes, you should cauterize with the cauteries that we have mentioned earlier, namely one cautery on the neck, two cauteries on the spine of the neck, six cauteries on the spine of the back, one large one on the hip and one smaller one, two on the shoulders, two on the hips, two on the shins, one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; beware of the nerves that are above the last rib, do not burn them; sometimes a person cauterizes a bone in the fist, and one in the stomach bone, and another in the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Know that the more you do cauterizing, the more help it provides, and it benefits him; know that the sick person does not feel pain from the cauterization as much as the healthy one does, because the body is already completely corrupted. It is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the ways of the irons. After curing the wound with flour several times with honey and other treatments until it heals.
de enfleure	inflammation
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When a swelling arises in any member and is treated with medicine, oils, and plasters, but it is not healed, then the cautery is applied on the limb according to its size and smallness; and the cautery may be shallow or deep into the flesh; then cure it with poultices until it is healed. And sometimes a cautery is made and in the hand, foot, back, at the nerve's exit that makes the limb immobile, thus removing the swelling; however, no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about members and the nerves moving the body.
de albaras	When a tumor appears on any member and it is treated with medicine, oils, and plasters, but it does not heal, then the cautery is made on the limb according to its size; and the cautery may be superficial or deep into the flesh; then cure it with poultices until it heals. And sometimes a cautery is performed in the hand, foot, back, at the nerve's exit that makes the limb immobile, thus removing the tumor; however, no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about members and the nerves moving the body.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease known as "albaras" grows, and the medicine does not work on it, then cauterize with a deep cautery until the blister disappears and its color changes; then treat with flour and lentils mixed with rose oil and banana leaves, along with cow blood and almond blood, each in equal parts; mix everything together and bind with cloth, and apply to the affected area until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure of scrofula by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When scrofula appears at the beginning and you want to stop it, if you cauterize it with a cautery that looks like a small circle all around the scrofula. And yet the wise ones say that one should cauterize in the middle of the scrofula; and yet this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it becomes ulcerated and corrupted, and I have seen it happen once; and a more correct thing is for it to be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circule", as we have said in our discussion of cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	the swelling that cannot grow or spread
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", which delays healing or because of its excessive growth or due to the age of the patient when they are decrepit (meaning very old) and have little blood, or because of time; and you see it hastening to heal: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries while pricking; afterwards leave it. For it will hasten to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced completely by the cautery, then heat the cautery according to this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of that disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the core, and make the cautery so that the patient feels it move out from their body in this way so that the course of the ulcer is evened out. Afterwards cure it until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure for fire with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another type of disease is called "corrodens", which is nothing but a corrosion of a limb, because it eats away at the limbs just as fire dries out wood. If you see this disease in a place where cauterization with fire can be used, then heat the cauterizers, both large and small, according to what is appropriate for the location or the sickness; after cauterizing all around until all the corruption is reached and nothing remains of it, remove everything that is corrupted. And then leave it for three days, and apply soft cauterized powder with oil until the burns from the fire are healed, and all the corruption. After the cure by burning ointments generates healthy tissue. If after three days you see that healthy tissue does not grow, that is good; if not, start cauterizing again on the parts that remain of the corrupted limb. This corrosion was sometimes cured with hot medicines instead of fire cauterization, but nonetheless fire cauterization is of greater help. I have already explained the cure for the disease caused by hot medicines in another section; take as much of it as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	the worms that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often times, a disease called "clos" arises in the feet according to our intention, which is a large swelling that hurts the foot. And the cauterization of this disease is according to two manners. This is to say, cauterization by fire, and cauterization by hot water. Cauterization by fire is that you heat one cautery, as a quill of a goose feather, and it should be made of good iron to the extent that it can pierce the nail on all sides, and that it has fine margins; afterwards, place it entirely hot on the nail, and turn your hand completely around the nail until it comes to the point of the nail; and leave it in this manner for four days until it begins to emit pus; then make a plaster of malicious herbs ground with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nails will shrink and be uprooted from their roots. Then heal the place with soothing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if it is converted on the outside of the body, and this happens often in hands and feet, then you should bring a hot water cauterization; and this is done in this manner: take a goat hair string or iron, or a quill of a goose feather, and place it on the nail and hold it, that is to say, to burn the warts; and place the string so that it encompasses entirely, then put a small amount of hot water in it, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the margin of the string comes to the root of the nail, and can find the hot water deep through to the root; and allow the patient a little bite of the hot water for an hour; then leave it as is, and it will uproot all its roots. Do this again, until you burn all those on the body, then heal them with ointments that soften the skin.
li cure dou trembler	the one who cures trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone trembles due to cold or fever of quartain, or from another [cause], it is necessary that you apply 4 or 5 cauteries along the spine of the back, 1 between each spine; and 1 cautery on the shank, and 1 on the stomach with an olive-leaf cautery; this will make him stop trembling, and hasten his recovery from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of rotten boils
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	Sometimes the body emits boils that are full of corrupt matter, if they appear at the beginning it is necessary to apply a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made from mirte stick or a long aristologue root, or an cautery lenticulaire. And sometimes they cauterize at the beginning when they appear, according to this method, and they cannot grow beyond that, but the superfluous matter is decomposed from which they come, and they are healed; however it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great outflows of blood from the cut artery at the wound that comes to the outside, or in the incision of an abscess, or in the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very bad thing to let it flow.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And even if it happens to anyone, hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein and hold it very tight so that the blood is stopped under your finger, and no more juice flows out; then take olive oil cauteries, both small and large ones until they are all red; then take .i., either large or small depending on the size of the wound and where the artery is running, and place the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery in place until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if a leap happens when you place your thumb over the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take immediately one other cautery that are by fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing one after the other until the vein is completely drained; and watch that you do not burn the nerve that is exposed, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when the vein dries up from the artery, it cannot be well stopped if the artery is large, except by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by strongly tied string, or by medicines placed on it that have the power to stop blood; and let it be tied and constricted accordingly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever brings a tightening of the ligature with cloth or puts something hot on it, or similar things, will not benefit if there is no profit.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone who has no mirror or medicine present, you should place your finger on the wound of the vein as we have said and stretch it out until it is tightened over the wound and the vein; and do not move it, but the cold moist should often be applied to make it very cold so that the blood congeals and thickens and remains; and make inquiries ahead about the person who needs cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of surgical treatments
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	In the first chapter we have told you about all diseases in which fire cautery or burning medicine is needed, and we have explained their uses, causes, instruments, forms of cauteries; and I have put that chapter up to the thighs and will proceed in this chapter by the same path for those things that are easier to understand.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauterizations, and for this reason greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	I advise you not to be foolish. For there are many ways that people come in for treatment. Some of them arrive with such illness that they die quickly due to the craziness that comes from their disease, and from the great severity of its malice; and of these one should be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these [people], he gives you his advice, and says: "Wait, I am cured"; and the sick person is stubborn. It is not appropriate that you agree with those who come to you who have this manner, but put more great consideration in your honor than in your desire, and do not open easily but wisely of those about which you are certain, and from which you can take and lose; and use prognostication and indication in the cures of your sick, so that health is converted; and this will help you to acquire good reputation, glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, Our Lords grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inspire with the holy inspiration of his hand, come.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Furthermore, I have divided this chapter into sections by chapters, according to what is before or in the chapter of cauteries, which I have described for you from head to feet, because you will find it easier to understand those matters which you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often comes to children during childbirth and when the head of the child is forced too hard; sometimes it happens because of reasons we do not know.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone other than children, and all those I have seen hurried towards death; therefore, it seems to me that I should waste less effort on such treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was full of water, and it grew larger every day until it could no longer support itself; and the moisture collected under the skull between the skin and the bone; and the treatments are such that if the moisture is between the skin and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make a large incision in the head; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture runs out; and here is the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you observe the edges where the abscess is located at each part, and when you press it with your hand inside, and it does not respond: then you must make four incisions in the middle of the abscess, according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture completely. After that, hold down the incisions with linen and powders, and put vinegar and oil on it, and leave it like that for five days; then open it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments, and keep the head stretched out gradually, and give the patient dry meat from a sheep's throat as much as necessary until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is that you look where the abscess is largest, and gather the pus; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Therefore, incise where the abscess is open, and drain the pus, and do as you can; but avoid covering the artery; and let blood flow, so that the patient dies a natural death from loss of blood and evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of scrofula
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When a certain disease called "cataract" affects the eyes or becomes worse, and medicine treatment is of no help, then the last resort is the cautery by cutting into the 2 arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Then, when you see them, have the patient bend his head backwards; afterwards wipe the skin of a rough cloth on the area where the arteries appear, then hold the patient's neck with one rough cloth; look for the artery openings, which are behind each ear, and place the pointed spatula (spatumile) on them; sign the edges, then cut one and the other with the sharp spatula as deep as to the bone, but not too close to the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it (the artery), push the spatula underneath the artery and cut through it (the artery).
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when a vein is cut, it jumps out continuously towards the top.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open on its own, then it is necessary to measure a distance of three fingers, then press and cut up to the bone; and it requires seven cubits (cubitus) or perhaps a little more or less according to what the patient can bear, and the filling of the artery; then observe the wound: if it remains above the bone without spitting out pus, then the cauterization performed does not reach it. Then hold the wound closed and bind it with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of emigration
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes with a sharp catarrh, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples and a feeble and aged headache, and it is treated by means of medicine cures but does not improve; then we should open the arteries of the temples and cauterize them as we have said.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extraction is that the patient leans backwards over his temples, and listens to the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well by beating, and is not easily retracted except in some cold-natured people; and if it has been retracted, the patient should tighten his neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth, and moisten the area with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatula of the following shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	then cut the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it up towards the tweezers and separate the cloths that are underneath each part; and if the artery is small, turn it to the point of the tweezers, then press that part according to the size of the two cheeks. For if it is not pressed, it will not open at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from the 5th finger joint, up to the 3rd joint; and if the arteries are large, you must tie it with a thick double silk thread so that pus does not come before the wound is closed, and there is bleeding; then cut off the excess between the 2 tendons at that hour itself, and if you see, cauterize the cauterizer scalpel up to the bone as much as the joints are cut; and this is the mutilation work, if the patient does not have fever and he is of a hot constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauteries is aid for finishing the sores: because it is of greater help to sores.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the extraction of arteries, one must fill the place with old cotton and put on tight bandages; and when you loosen them, cure it with dry medicines that make pus, and bandages, until it is healed; and if there is no incision of the artery as much as you work, hurry to cover it with cauterization, or use vitriol and strain it with your hand so that the wound does not become infected; and if you do not have this present, put your finger on the place until it freezes, and scrape the place with cold water until it stops, and strained as necessary; and the mutilated and easier in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein of this sharp cautery with two parts, but they should be well thickened to keep longer its heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	When the instrument (strumens) is too thin, it retains less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And should have between the two blades, one thick of space, and when you have marked with incision on both sides, and you place the heated iron for as long as it comes to the bone, and cut the vein in two leagues; and they should be kept apart because they are not welded from this cautery throughout; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes flow out of the veins that are on top of the face near the head, and no medicine helps in treating it, you see the patient's face turning pale with shivering, as if with fever; and when they are tender and moist so that the eyelashes fall off, the eyelids are scalded by the tears, then this kind of treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they called it the "contused cure" in ancient times, which means you make incisions on both sides of the patient's forehead equally according to the length of the forehead, and one of the incisions should be as deep as two fingers downward along the forehead, and the others should be .iij. inches apart above the eyelids, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are on both sides above the eyelids; also keep your hand away from the continuation of both jaws, and each wound should be the size of three fingers joined together;
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	and prepare a piece of sponge and a lot of bandages to absorb the blood, then insert the sharp stick (spatula) from this shape:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision which is across the temple up to the second incision; and scrape all the fat that is between the two cuts right to the bone, then do another thing from the mid-incision up to the other second one, and then pull out this spathule.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	Insert the instrument called "cultellaire" into the first incision. It is very sharp on one side and soft but not sharp on the other, and it has this shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the cutting side towards the fat, and the soft side towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the mid-incision. Cut all the vessels that run from the eye to the hair as long as the incision is continuous until it opens the fat, and then do another thing in the mid-incision up to the other end; and then equalize the blood and express the fat for the blood taken; then put a piece of old cotton cloth in each incision, and put damp linen cloths soaked in vinegar, oil, and asafetida on top, and ensure that no pus comes out; on the third day remove the stitches, and apply a large plaster of strong ointment of basilicon with rose oil, and other treatments for wounds until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	The root of the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	Whenever a sharp catarrh commonly comes, you see the thin and small hairs, dimming the vision, and burned paper; and the hair follicles itch, and where the head is painful with severe pain, and the patient coughs; then know from these symptoms that those substances and the catarrh do not come from anywhere other than many veins, and the cure for this is to open them.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you should command the patient to recline his head, then make a large incision at the back of the head, and another one wide. [i.e., two incisions]. Start from the incision of the left temple to the right temple, and let the incision reach the bone; keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move while eating; when the bone is exposed, suck out all the blood with a sponge, then squeeze between the two lips of the incision and put old cotton in it, and bind it with linen thread; then cover it with wet cloths soaked in wine and oil, and be careful not to cause an abscess to form; when the bone is removed, you must rub the bone until char flesh begins to grow, then treat it with things that promote growth of flesh.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take 2 parts of wheat flour and 4 parts of colophony, and make a poultice with it; administer it in these wounds to alleviate pain everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stoppage of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of the four things: grains, animals, stones or similar such as iron; seeds like peas, beans, lentils; liquid substances like water and oils and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When a stone or anything falls into the ear that does not fit snugly or grow in the ear, and it does not adhere to the ear, put the ear towards the sun. If you see the stone, distill a little purple oil or camphor oil, then administer extraction; and make the patient cough with congee, and block the nostrils when the coughing occurs, and place pieces of fabric or wool around the ear; and hold it upwards. Many times farting occurs through this cure; and if it does not occur, administer extraction with fine tweezers as shown in the following form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out at the hinges, that's good; if not, introduce extraction with a thin wire of small twisting; and if it doesn't jump out by that means, make a thread of wax and push the head of the thread or ear canal firmly, and stop up what is around the thread with soft wax so that the vein cannot enter with the thread; then pull forcefully, for many times it comes out as we have said; and if it doesn't come out in this manner, take glue from where you can get it, put any tool suitable for this purpose on it, and put a piece of cotton around it; then press the glue onto the stone or something similar and pull forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it doesn't jump out by any of the things we have said, hurry to incise the ear before an abscess forms and spasms; and the manner of incision is that you first cleanse the patient's head, then draw blood according to the strength of its virtue, then seat the patient between your hands and turn the ear upward, and make a small incision in the root of the ear where the fat or flesh hangs; and let the incision be like a moon, until you reach the bone, then break it as far as your power allows, and suck the pus quickly into your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that swells and it cannot be extracted, introduce one thin and subtle spatula in this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And make an incision in that grain. But do not do so if you think the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then strain it with subtle tweezers and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the ear that drips water, the patient should first use warm mustard poultice and stuff the ear with old cotton. The patient should lie on their side over the affected ear. If it jumps out due to this, that's good. If not, take several small and light pieces of stone according to the size of your finger, heat them slightly in fire; then have the patient put one end of a thin stick in the ear and hold another piece of wood over the stone in the ear; continue striking stone against stone until the water jumps out completely, and it should jump out fully; and if you observe, take a piece of thread, push one end into the ear, and the other end hold near fire until the thread closest to the ear is burnt; then repeat this process with more threads until the water has jumped out completely, as we have said in the above passage.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an animal, if it has a small body like fleas and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it has a large body that can be felt, use the extraction method with tweezers; it is easier to remove lighter objects from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in treating distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if any worms appear, take them with fine tweezers, and if none appear, take a reed of this shape.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And make it narrow within and wide without. And push the most subtle tip into the ear according to the degree of suffering of the patient, then suck out completely the reed; do this often until all the worms come out. And if they do not come out, stop up the reed with cotton as I said in the previous section; and if they do not swell out as we have said, administer distillations that the ancients have proven effective in the treatment of worms, and you will find them or treat distillations; and if you distill your oils and medicines into the ear using this apparatus as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And make it of silver or tin narrow within and wide above to distill; and for pressing inside the distillation, one instrument made of tin is required; and if you see, take a grater and wrap it around the tip with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you have in the reed, and the reed should be in the ear; then push the grater with all the cotton inside, and press your hand evenly until the oil is distilled or boils out of the ear; and let the patient smell it within, and the distillation should be one pot heated by fire in this way that it is distilled in the ear; and ensure that it is not too cold, for the medicines will not be as effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the stoppage of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some imperfection in the ears; and this same thing happens to men by stoppage of a wound or pus coming from within the ear, and this stoppage comes completely into the ear at times when it cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a drop or two of pus protruding, and it can be clearly seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, if it comes completely into the ear and cannot be seen, it is difficult to cure in various conditions, and in such cases, you must place the sick person's ear in the sun; look inside: if you see the obstruction clearly, open the affected area with this spatula-like tool that is shaped as shown below:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be cauterized and incised all around, both in front and behind, so that it does not touch the ear; if the swelling is of new flesh or cartilage of the ear, hold it with subtle forceps and strike gently until the flesh is completely burned out.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If the swelling is deep in the ear, take a subtle razor and scald slightly with fire, then place it against the cartilage of the ear. If you feel the swelling, causing pain to the patient's hearing, pierce gently, ensuring not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put a linen patch according to the size of the wound in the ear and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound heals; take a linen patch and moisten it with rosewater, and sprinkle powder of vitriol over it; if you see the ear swelling, it is necessary to remove the linen patch and apply another moistened linen patch made of rose oil and beeswax until the swelling subsides; then heal it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding, which are either to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper charcoal
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This althelul that comes from the hairs when they are moist and dry, it is necessary to stretch them with tongs and tweezers, and then crush them with a spatula of their roots; then put vitriol powder on the place.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And without removing [the affected part], if you cauterize with the subtle cautery of lenticles, and after incision is necessary to be cauterized; and many times they heal, since nothing remains from their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the hailstone
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope. se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	Many times hail-like things come on paper with a condition resembling hail in shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "grandine," which is a collection of thick moisture on the upper and lower layers of the paper; the procedure is as follows: take care to ensure that the hail does not move from one side to another, and it is an easy thing to know; then make an opening, followed by scraping off each part gently, then grasp with pincers and squeeze. If you cannot cover it without piercing the paper slightly, do not worry the patient; if the tear is large, assemble it with a stitch and heal until it is healed; but if it is small, do not apply force because the liniments restore it soon and cause pain.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the stone is descending inside the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper and place the stone in tweezers, press it from both sides; and if the paper is pushed back by the incision, it does not matter; and when the stone is pressed, apply oil of brine to the affected area, and treat the wound of those who are injured until the patient recovers.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat from the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil. Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	Exinach is a fat that is rendered in cloth from the abovementioned papers, and this happens more often in children than in adults, and it causes great discomfort to their eyes, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears quickly flow into their eyes; and for this reason, they lie down on their faces immediately and sleep, and their papers are moistened beneath their eyelids covered with exinach which opens in oil. And when you press the affected area with your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the method of work is that the patient places their head on your lap; and then take one linen cloth and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the size required for each part, then place it over [them]; and press with your hands from both sides so that the parts are assembled within the circle; then make an incision in the middle of the moist area with a sharp spatula, and it should not be larger than the wound made during vein opening; and cut through the skin completely to expose the incised area; and in various positions the incised area comes from the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Then take a piece of coarse cloth between your hands and spread it apart until it is scattered; and ensure that you do not widen the incision or bring the spatula to the oil, do not pierce it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	If the incised area does not open at the beginning of the incision, raise it slightly; then spread it as we have said, then wet cloths with oil and water, and place them on the wound, and hold bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree. Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if such men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains, then heal it until it is clean. And if an abscess heats up at its place, then treat with plasters soothing it until it is clean.
des poilz des papieres	of the papers' hairs
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper grows hairs other than its nature, and is nurtured, it harms the eyes, and brings about manners of diseases such as the accustomed tears and swelling of papers and albugine, to the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to four methods: either by cautery with fire, or by medicine for ague according to that which is before in the chapter on cautery, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by canes, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must place the patient's head on your sound side, then turn the paper with the oil on your left hand; if it is converted (turned), that's good; if not, push an awl through one filament (hair strand) of it; and cut the hair adjacent to the hair strands, and draw one filament above the entire paper, then scrape it flat; then make a hole in the part underneath the paper, beneath the hair, all the way from the large fold to the small; then extract one filament, and place a small tent of cotton and linen beneath the paper, then mark on the paper a figure like the thorn of blackberry, and note that the figure should be according to the quantity that you see will raise the paper which has been designated for all.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les .ij. lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des .ij. angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout .i. fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les .ij. sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a .iij. jors ou .iiij.; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor;	And if you need to apply a large amount of paper according to the softness of the paper; then make a hole along the entire span of the two lines that you have marked, and begin from the large fold to the small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hair in the thickness of a root, then insert the onion into one of the angles of the key, then peel it all; then sew the two lips together with a needle and thread of fine wool, and squeeze out the blood, and tie up the excess hairs above the two scissors with any adhesive substance, if you wish to do this; and if not, do not care about it, then leave the suture and the hairs until 2 or 4 days; then treat the wound without suture with drying and constricting substances, as the paper will heal at the edge of the wound and its assembly, but the suture is rotten (as they say in the old), and this is a risky procedure.
et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a .iij. oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	and if you use another method: it is that you mark the paper with a figure like the thorn of blackberry, as we have said, with four openings according to the shape shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then bind (or tie) equally the parts which are above the small ones, according to the form shown here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait .i. fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute .i. autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans;	And if you do not have the ability to hold the pliers, and the parts are not equal, take a needle with one thread, and stick it into the figure; and insert another thread of the large one through the great incision, and the second thread through the small one, and assemble the threads equally between your fingers; then move your hand equally, and move all the skin so that you have signed it, as we have said, then sew together the two edges of the wound with stitching, and heal it until it is healthy; and if an abscess comes to your incision, calm it with ointment and similar soothing balms.
et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And sometimes the hair of the papyrus is converted, which requires you to use what we have said about incision; however, stitching in one and the other is more artful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for canines is as follows: You should fold the paper and place it inside as I have said, then make two canines by art, and two subtle threads of the same length as the paper and the width of a needle hole; take the two heads from two parts where you hold the threads; then put one on top of the other subtly over what is above the paper of oil, and bind the two canines from the two parts; leave it in this state for some days, and the skin that is bound will die and rot away, until it falls off.
S’il tarde, si le cope aunes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des .ij. cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes time, if you have to force it, then treat it until it heals completely; and when the wound is closed, and no more hairs can be felt, and this is the form of the two canines that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The workings are as follows: You take a fine needle and insert one thin thread of silk; then assemble the heads and place them together subtly, and make sure that the length of the threads is about one palm (5 inches); then tie another fine silk thread briefly to the end of the canine; then place the patient's head in your hand and ensure that the work is done in the sun, as this is a subtle and delicate procedure; then insert the needle into the entire sheath next to the natural hair root and pierce the paper immediately so that it pulls up the natural hair; then pull out the hair until it reaches the end of the canine, and put that hair in the canine, if there is one or more; then pull your hand until the hairs come out completely with the natural hair in the paper.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the shot (arrow or other projectile) is expelled but the hairs do not come out with it, you shall draw the shot beneath to its full length that you have ordered, until the shot comes forth through the wound and you see it by the sight of the eye; then, you shall draw out the shot and the string, close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair regrows in its place and flesh grows over it; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from a goat's beard with it, and let it be grown along with that which you leave, until it is distanced and then cut it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the purulence of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease called "aleacrati" or purulence comes in the eye, it happens in two ways: natural and unnatural. It occurs suddenly due to injury, wound, cut, or similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	And the method of work in it is that you cut the joint, separate the sides of it, put thread soaked in flax within it and bind it until it heals; and do not use drying and constricting agents in its treatment. For if you do this, the illness returns worse than before; but for this kind of work, use softening items, such as fenugreek; boil flaxseed and linseed oil, strain it and wrap a linen cloth around it, and treat with this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.
