And the key to your treatment is to ensure that the joint does not heal in its former shape; and this work that we have mentioned has no effect on this illness unless it corrects its shape so that it does not return to its former state.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the fat from the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens. Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait .i. fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en .ij. chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a .i. spatumile large.	This disease that is below, which is truly called "axacrati", and is both natural and accidental. The accidental part comes from wounds and cuts and cauterization and similar things; the method of treatment in it is that you take a needle with double thread and stick it in the flesh, and make it pierce from the left tear duct to the right one, so that the threads come out in two joints of the flesh; then place the flesh over the whole needle, and the handle at a distance of one spatumile.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren .i. raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent .ij. fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des .ij. fendures des .ij. angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «.j. griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les .ij. parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the figure of the stone returns according to what is required, that's good; if not, take a rasp and place it in the wound, and turn the stone, and make two wounds where the stone lies within the flesh; and let the joints of the two wounds be at the angles of the incision you made, and make one angle so that when they are assembled, the figure is like the figure of a letter with no "I" Greek; then remove that flesh, according to the thickness it protrudes below the stone, and join the two detached parts with linen thread; then treat as we have said for the medicines softening and ointments until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a wound or stitching or cauterization, it is necessary that you make a deep incision under the hair of the paper, as mentioned before; then separate between the two layers of linen, as I have said; and the work should be done according to the shape of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise masters prepare any tool with all possible means to return the figure to its natural shape; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for the work and tools in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	Sudden blow of paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suture happens in the hands of men in such a manner that the paper above is glued with white oil and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the point of a razor beneath the paper, lift it up; and hold it with pincers, until you reach that which is at the root of the splinter, which should not be too sharp nor too jagged, so that the patient does not suffer from too sharp a splinter piercing the oil; and your incision, from which you scrape away the assembled mass, should be gentle, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and this entire assembly is healed, and at times it becomes infected with foul oil and produces pus and colic; then put between the paper and the oil a tent of linen, and place on the oil damp wool in abundance of egg; and after the third day use warm colic and healing ointments until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the nail of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	Know that the nail is of two types: one is nervous and resembles a hard horn, and another which is not nervous but resembles white frozen moisture; when it is touched by iron and cooked with tweezers, it cannot move; and both types begin towards the large root and grow little by little until they cover the entire nail bed and light and the movement of oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient places his head in your hand, then you open the eyes; take paper with your hand, then grasp the nail with tweezers of small double curvature and hold it above; then take a needle, put a horse hair or cow or bull hair and a strong thread on it; double the tip of the needle a little and pierce it into the nail, and poke it all through, tie the nail with the thread and hold it above, and shave off all the hair from the side of the nail that was under the cuticle and the silk to the hair up to the root, then crush the rest in the root of the big toe to a very subtle paste with small forceps, and leave the natural flesh or root, so that the corpuscles do not flow out as is customary; and sometimes the nail grows only at the onychium (the upper part of the nail) and along the sides, as we have said; then shave off all the substance of it in this way:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatumile does not touch the flesh and tear it apart, and that the pulp is not pierced; and after the incision, pour a little oil of sebum (oily matter secreted by skin glands) and collyrium (medicine used for eye problems), and leave it until the next day; then cure it as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nerveous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the unguent can't enter, this resemblance of a nail is often cured with medicines; and they grow as I have told in the division, and if you see it covered, it works the oil of the patient, and take the spatulum lightly and sharp according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	Gently press the nail above, and if you see that it does not soften and reason does not apply to it, distill from your mouth into the colyrium oil made of litargirio and red collyrium powder and sulfur, and let the oil rest until the next day; then repeat the work according to this same process until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing opposes in the oil, as with an abscess, then let it drain, and cure the abscess hot until it is healed, then repeat the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh around the armpit harms in oil greatly, suspend it at the onion, and cut a part of it but not all, so that no tears come from it; then distill in the oil colyrium red which is made with litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that arises above the eyelid
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tune bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre;	Sometimes red flesh grows in the eyes of some men, covering the eyelid and pressing against the paper and turning towards the outside, looking like a rosebud; and the treatment for this is that the patient places his head in your lap, then you open the eyes, and take off all the red flesh as far as the appropriate incisions according to what follows in this chapter, holding it with force; then cut the first piece of red flesh, and continue cutting until finished, making sure not to harm the oil at the work; and make the incision with a spatula as we have said in the incision of the nail and with the small instruments of which one removes the seed, as the form after this chapter demonstrates.
et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	And when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, apply oil of turpentine or distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines, put cotton soaked with egg white on top to ensure that it is hot; if anything remains, and the wound becomes inflamed, and you doubt about the heat of the incision, leave the oil and treat the abscess with cooling medicines; then return to your work until it is healed, and do this with every char that is treated in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary that you alleviate the cure of each oil with a natural remedy; and for an accidental treatment, in work with iron; do not put your hand in any of these treatments until you see that this member is strong enough for that work.
des voines des eulz	veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors. Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	When the veins are red and covered with oil, they appear to perform their work and weaken the oil for all days. Therefore, it is necessary that you first examine if the oil, in which the vein is located, is indeed the problem, and not another disease; then proceed as follows: instruct the patient to place his head on your healthy surface, then suspend those veins completely according to your wisdom, and let the incisions be subtle doubled according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two incisions by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then carefully apply force to those veins subtly, and squeeze the blood out hour after hour, until you see the veins move away from the oil; also ensure that the oil is not pricked by the tips of the lancets, and perform this task at noon in front of the sun, and be very diligent in your work so as to not spoil the veins; and when you have completed this, if it distills green and red collyrium for correcting those that remain affected by the sebel.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot catch [or bind] all of it in that hour, make a plaster on the oil of soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and assured of healing, then resume according to this manner which is beforehand until it is healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the fistula (small tube) of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire (a cyst or abscess) is called "arissati" fistula: when you treat it with cautery and burning medicine as I said before, and it is not healed, there is a device within it that you should cut open on the abscess where it must break, and drain all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and blackness, if [the area] is ready with all the instruments as mentioned here; it is called "sharp head", and make a hollow [cavity] of about 1 inch deep, pointed like a chisel as shown in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Then turn the bone corruption between your hands and press with your hand slightly to ensure that the corruption is removed; do this once, then restore the joint with medicinal poultice.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi xl. jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent .i. foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a .iij. angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the joint is swollen and pus forms, and the back of the bone is swollen and remains so for 40 days without improving or abscessing, and it appears healthy; if not, there is no other means except to bring the fistula to the surface of the neck as shown in this form: you should expose the bone a second time with an iron, and with medicines that burn, and when exposed, take one awl according to this form, and let the head of the iron be at four angles, and the shaft be slender up to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil .i. poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone of the ulna (a forearm bone), and move your hand away from the oil or marrow. Then turn the drill completely until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it if they hold their hand on their elbow; and then restore the joint with dry medicines as I have taught you, and when the flesh hardens and strengthens the joint, the matter goes to the elbow; it is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	The translation of this line is: "of the oil's discharge" or "from the discharge of the oil".
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eye is completely open and there is no need to disturb the nose or reduce it, you must hold the patient; then clean the eye, then apply poultices or hot oil to help heal, then place the oil (a mixture of aconite, aloe, incense, and sarcolocca) on a linen thread and tie the eye, then apply ointment on bands and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths, fold each one in four, and then place one on top of another according to the amount needed by the eye; then tighten with a strong bandage and repeat the poultices to help heal without hurting; then remove the poultices and leave the tied eye for a day and night, and if the thread wears out, you must tie it tightly again; then remove the thread after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not; repeat the ointment, cloths, thread, and poultices until the eye is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	The dislocation of a torn membrane
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in a torn membrane, they open up and fart like paper, similar to grains of resin and are visible; then you must cover it. The procedure is such that you insert an awl into the root of the affected area until it reaches above, then insert another awl where there is a double thread from the edge of the tear; pierce it, leaving the first awl in place according to its position; then tie the end of the double thread and wrap a part of the membrane around it, tightening it, then remove the awl and apply oiled linen cloth moistened with egg; leave it until the threads grow with the membrane, then cure the area with comforting substances until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is held closed by the membrane on both sides in a circular bandage of fabric until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear large, pierce it with a fine spatula coming from oil and remove the moisture and pus, then enter immediately; then pull out until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	From the bone of the oil (can mean "from a bone soaked in oil")
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de .ij. pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit. si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee .i. poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not found in any bone other than the one assembled in oil, resembling an abscess draining, but it is not an abscess; and the method of its appearance in the work is that you make the patient sit on a chair equipped and upright. Then take his head between your hands with two parts, and move him until you see the bone come up to your eyes. Then pierce it, and do not drain and open the lumen, and let the patient see things as he usually does; and if it does not drain below, know that it is an abscess, and if the emergence of the bone is not prepared as we have said, make the patient sit between your hands. Then take the fine spatula and put it under the horny membrane .i. piece along the continuation of the conjunctive with the horny membrane and the corona, until the bone comes out; and when it is issued, let it distill into hot oil mixed with honey or fenugreek boiled in honey, then cure it with another treatment until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	diseases of the oil (can mean "diseases that occur from bones soaked in oil")
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit. Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre. se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	1. We have the appearance of the eyes in division, and what is necessary for piercing; do this according to health. You must make the patient sit between your hands crossed, away from light due to sunlight, and press the holy oil strongly onto him and hold it tight; then put paper soaked with the oil on your left hand if the eye is on the left side, or on your right hand if the eye is on the right side; then take in your right hand (if the eye is on the left side) the instrument called "almagda", or take it in your left hand (if the eye is on the right side); then place the tip of the instrument under the crown through the thickness of a finger into that part of the oil at the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument named "almagda" vigorously and hold your hand steady until it pierces the oil, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be at the full measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the iris; and this is the crown of the eye; then you will see the bone in the paper due to the clarity of the perforated fabric, and then put the instrument until it reaches the place where the eye is, then press it along another path. If the eye comes out now, the patient sees it before him and the instrument in its oil.
Aprés repose .i. petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens. Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.  Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	After a short rest and if the eye returns to its second path, place force with the instrument, and when it is well fixed and does not rise again, gently rotate almagda around your hand little by little; then put a small amount of gemstone oil inside. Then pour in oiled cloth or damp linen soaked in rose oil and abundant egg, and bind it with holy oil. We, and those who are of our time, place on top a mixture ground with abundant egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have too hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit", which is shaped as follows:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai .i. leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide .i. dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en .j. leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce only the conjunction (suture), and do not go too deep, but make .i. (one) thin incision, then apply the ointment, as we have said; and for the completion of the work arrange the patient to lie on his back in .j. (two) dark rooms; and be careful of all movements, and take light foods, and do not move his head neither to the right nor to the left, and bind him according to his disposition until three days; then unbind him in the same dark room, and test his sight, and make him see some things, and then rebind him for up to seven days; and you should not perform this, except during the cure or after the incision, but you should alleviate it, because the pain increases rapidly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice .i. orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse. Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	If abscesses come up, you must unbind the oil before the seventh day, and direct the one who soothes the abscess; and when it is soothed, then uncover the eye and put on it .i. (one) linen cloth to cover for any day, and be there in the dark room. Then slowly leave the house, bit by bit, and return to his cases; and know that no disciples should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Iram, who told us that in his land they pierce almond ointment, so that the pain subsides, but I never saw anyone do it in our land, nor have I ever read it in books of ancient times; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the resemblances of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them see them; and they are from a rain properly speaking:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And be the heads of these from the same subtlety, and the rear parts in four angles pointed.
de la char sor le neis	from the flesh on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	At times, diverse charities that resemble scorpions in their base are born; and if there are such [charities], or if a char is swollen of a dark color, and if a char is soft with a good color. In those cases of the soft char, but not swollen, you must make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and spit the urine on these charities, and pull them out; then catch what you can hold with the sharp subtle spatula until you know that this char is completely removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be caught, open it with all sorts of subtle instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if the abscess is swollen, or an arrow, seek aid as necessary; and if these are malignant abscesses, hasten and cauterize until the wound is sealed and all charities are removed, then spit bile or hot vinegar or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	If the abscess does not open and moisture goes up to the mouth, know that it is healthy; if moisture does not drain as necessary, know that there is pus in the bone above, so instruments do not come for cutting: then you should insert a thick thread of linen, coated with oil or wax, between each stitch about one finger's width, and have the patient hold the threads inside his mouth as far as he can, and pull until the pus comes out through the nose; children in school often do this, and it is easy for someone who wants to do it. Hold the head that comes from the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and know each other's position while we are inserting the thread. Do this until you know that the threads have corrupted the pus, then pull out the thread, drain the pus, soak the thread in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the abscess as before; do this for four days or more, until the ointment has dissolved all of the remaining pus; then place a plank of wood near the abscess for several days until it is healthy, and if there is need for drying medications, use them. This is the form of the instrument to purge the head, as oil and medicines are distilled through the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it shall be of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a cane, and lead it thus; and if you see, make a closed cane, and let the tool be plain for purging the head; and have one handle on the head for holding when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the chest on the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a disease named "telul" arises on the neck of the head and grows large over time until it is visible; therefore, it is necessary to treat it from the beginning, remove all pus, and then apply fire cautery or burning medicine to it; if it is not treated promptly when it first appears, and it becomes hard, dark, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an aggravated abscess, for when it is touched even once, the patient experiences great harm; and if the abscess is soft in texture but does not have a foul color, you can cover it entirely, let the patient relax without fear, and treat the surrounding area with drying and constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nails are cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If inflammation of continuation comes in one of these cartilages, it helps little, except in some men. Therefore, when this occurs in any case, you should examine if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring the two lips together to a stitch, then heal it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated from one side and the other, you must cauterize all the parts of them where there is pain, then bring the two lips together to a stitch, tighten it, and sprinkle powder of dragon's blood, and incense ground; and place the powders on a piece of plaster of strong or another plaster adhering, and let it stay until it heals by itself, then heal it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is such that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as I have told you in abdominal stitching; or with thread, as I have mentioned before.
des apostemes des levres	for abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	When abscesses occur within the lips that are hard and grain-like, either small or large, then you must turn the lips and cut through each side with scissors and take it out with tweezers in each part; afterwards apply vitriol powder to the incision until the wound is cauterized; and then apply alum to heal the wound of dry things until it becomes healed.
de la char des gencives	of the flesh of the jaws
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often flesh grows adjacent to the jaws that the ancients call "albulus"; it must be held with tongs and cut at its root, leaving the vein or blood to flow; then apply vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders on the place; and if the flesh returns after incision, which often happens, cut it a second time and cauterize it: it does not return again after cauterization; and these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	boils
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes, teeth or gums assemble together at the jaw, inside the mouth between the gums; these are ugly and rough; and sometimes the tooth is black and citron colored and sharp, until corruption comes to the gum, and the tooth is foul-smelling; then you must make the patient sit between your hands, and his head should be in your lap, and peel back the teeth or the roughness that appears, as long as nothing remains; and in this way do with the blackness and the greenness, and the yellow and other stains, until they are removed; and if one removes what is at the root first, it is good; if not, then begin again the second day and the third, as long as you have everything removed; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for cleaning, according to the work that shows, because the cleaner who cleans the teeth has other forms than the one who cleans between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you are treating the tooth from its pain, it is necessary that you pull slowly as much as you can, for this should not be done hastily; for this is a very high substance until there is no excuse to scrape.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Then when the patient is constrained to pull, it is necessary that you are certain about which tooth needs pulling. Many times, the pain deceives the patient and thinks that it is a healthy tooth, and pulls the good one; but the pain does not depart at all until the bad one is removed, as we have seen in the past; and when you are absolutely sure of which tooth needs pulling, then you should scrape around the tooth everywhere. Use strong spatumile to protect the gums from all sides; then move it to your hands or subtle tenailles at the very tip and tip, until they are completely loosened, then tighten the tenailles firmly; and let the patient's head be in your lap and hold him so that he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After straightening the tooth without breaking it, if it does not come out by itself, take one of these instruments and gently push it in from each side, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is pierced and eaten, it is necessary to fill it with bandages where the perforation is; and hold it delicately with pliers so that it does not break when pulled; and it must be operated very carefully around the gumline to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take good care not to break it, and if a part remains in the patient due to the root causing greater pain than the first. And take care not to do as foolish lords often do, who by their haste and recklessness sometimes break the cart, and never bring what we have described; but sometimes they cause great disease through the roots that remain or through the cartilage that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is pulled, wash the area with wine or vinegar and oil, and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, use vitriol powder; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, which initially silence the teeth, should be long points and thick handles, so that they do not twist when you pull the tooth; and these are their forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be large members which do not yield when drawn, and let them be made of hard iron and sharp-edged to hold fast.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains when pulled, then you must place cotton wool soaked in butter on it for 1 or 2 days until the tooth loosens, then insert the tongs called "algefri", which look like a surgical probe; and inside them make holes as with a chisel and this is its shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, you must cut open the skin all around the root, and put the instrument called "althali," which is known as a pincers, there; this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	It should be large and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through these tongs, that is good; if not, help with all the instruments, and here are the shapes that follow:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument with two prongs, here is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are in front of the teeth, and of this tool that seems like large pincers, whose shape is:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this tool should not break, and know that many instruments of teeth are; and likewise other instruments which are not counted; and the wise masters skillfully find their own tool according to what their work and the sickness show, for there are such diseases where the ancient ones did not teach any instrument due to diversity among them; and if it breaks a chariot or another bone that it could have healed, then search for the instruments that are needed, which I told you, and help with gestures, of which this is the shape:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and well-holding to hold the bone, so that it does not slip, but can hold and remove; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is pus in the bone, which is small, grind all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not as natural according to the body, and the shape is ugly, even in virgin women, then you must know that if the tooth has not erupted after the tooth, and it is not in the correct place, and it cannot be straightened or filed: then file it; and if it is near the tooth, take this instrument with the following form, and resembling a small beak, made of sharp metal at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the coping file should be used with much care for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can file it, then file it with a small file like this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the file used to make needles; and with a light touch file the tooth little by little, so that it does not move too much when it emerges; then smooth the end in any way with any smoother, and if the tooth is excessively sharp and it bites the tongue, then you must file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bite the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth fall out
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the teeth fall out either by being knocked out or falling off, and the patient cannot press them back in place so they do not fall again, and you treat them with medicines that restrain, it does not work; instead, you must tie them up with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and rot, but gold threads never do. The thread should be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the space between the teeth. And if you see that the teeth are moving, take the thread and double it between two healthy teeth, then place the pliers between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more of them, as long as you can see clearly up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then cover again up to the part where you started, and hold your hand delicately and carefully, so that they do not move. Make sure your knot is at the root of the tooth so that it does not escape. Then take the pliers with the thread and assemble them, and place them back in their original position, making sure they do not bite the tongue; then leave them like this as tight as possible for as long as they can stay in place, and if they slip or the thread breaks, tie them up again with another thread. If they remain in place and serve for a period of time, it is the form of the teeth and the method of the alignment of the two healthy and two loose teeth, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the teeth fall out and are put back in their place, freshly, as we have said; and do not let anyone interfere who is not wise and patient, and sometimes a tooth of bone from a cow or other animal is made and placed where the missing tooth was, and it is tied in as described above, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cover the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Sometimes, this ligament under the tongue occurs naturally or by accident due to a wound. The procedures are such that you open the mouth of the patient, hold his head steady, and lift the tongue; then cover the nervous ligament with a broad bandage, until the tongue is dislocated from its position, and if there is hardness or knotting, and it is due to sudden injury, press the incisors and cover that area with a broad bandage; ensure that the wound is not too deep, as there is an artery beneath it. Once done, lift up the swelling with warm rose water or cold water. Then put a linen tent over the tongue. Make him bite it every night to prevent healing. If bleeding occurs, apply vitriol powder. If the bleeding continues, cauterize with a slow cautery, which is good for this purpose; then treat it with other medicine until he is cured.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you see it of a thin color or black or hard, such that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it is spreading towards blanchor, and there is moisture, apply the incisors, and free it with a slender spatula from both sides. And if bleeding continues at your work, apply vitriol powder until it stops. Then return to your work until you remove all pus. Then lift up the swelling with warm rose water or cold water and treat it with other medicines until it is cured.
des apostemes de la gorge	From the abscess of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Sometimes come within the throat boils called "godath", which are properly called the two almonds. When you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess of small size and light color, do not touch it with iron. And if it is red and the base is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the flow of blood; but let it be until it is ripe, and then you will cut it open or it will burst by itself; and if it is of white color again, and the base is thin, prepare the instrument for covering, but first check if the abscess is calm and appeased. Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his head should be in your hand, and open the mouth and take the sergeant between his hands, and press the tongue under all the instrument, as follows; it is of silver or subtle iron like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue to all this instrument, and if you see the abscess, take the hook and poke it into the almond, and pull it up more than you can; and pull anything from the cloth with it, then strike it on the instrument, as follows, which resembles a forceps; and even though the head is curved, one side to the other, and they are very sharp, and made of iron or brass:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the iron with pliers, of which form follows:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument present, hold the iron with pliers, of which form follows:
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, namely one of small size; and I had tightly closed the entire throat, so that the woman could not exhale through the narrowed passage, and could not eat or drink, and would have died if she had lasted for a day or two. The abscess was so high up that it had been placed two fingers deep into the throat. I hastily cut through it, and pulled out a large piece of pus; then I closed the other opening in the throat, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after cutting through the abscess again, I took part of it, and no more pus came out than a small amount of blood; and thus the passage in the throat was unblocked for the woman, and she began to drink hot water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away at the abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, and filled the space that I had vacated, becoming very large; then I tricked it and cauterized it inside her throat: in this way the growth ceased; and I left those parts alone, and only God knew what happened to them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the eye swells and becomes long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not help, and you see that the abscesses are soothed, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and if it is large and rounded and not long; and it is bloody or of dark color or black, then you must make an incision in it. For there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it as described, according to the shape and size, you should have the patient sit facing the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument mentioned earlier in this treatise; then insert the probe into the eye, pull it out, and cut it in .i. or 2 places as I said in the incision of the 2 almonds. And do not make an incision beyond the natural limit; for if you do, it causes pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what was said in the incision of the 2 almonds, and treat it until it is healed. And if the patient fears the cutting, then you should use an instrument for cauterization to lessen fear. The manner of cauterization is sharp heat. It is that the patient places their head on your lap, and then presses the tongue with the instrument mentioned in this chapter on cauterization, and press it with hot coals, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and use the handle of this instrument, which has the following form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And have a hair or oil pot where one puts the medicine, like the scoop of a spoon, and place the instrument on top of all the medicine over the eye; and let the patient lie on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth into the medicine without it descending to the throat or the nose; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye for the amount of half an hour, until you see the pus and the inflammation of the medicine are soothed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument into the sheath over the wound, until the cotton adheres to the eye; and do this repeatedly, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry for 4 or 5 days. And if you need to restart the cauterization with the medicine, restart it, and after the cauterization drain the pus around the eye with cotton wrapped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and wash it with cold water and heal it with gargarisms until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective by fumigation than by cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this manner, take camomile, yarrow, origanum, rue, and wormwood, and assemble them all or some of them in one pot, and place it on a fire to boil; the pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and in the pot have one opening covered with fine cloth in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And be it of silver or tin, and let one of the eyes be pushed into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the tube while the eye is being mortified; afterwards repeat often, as long as the eye dries out, and ensure that you do not start this at the beginning of the abscess's heating up, for many things may happen then; and do not use this unless it is during the declination of the abscess's heating. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put an eggshell crack inside the patient's mouth so that the patient does not have too much heat in the mouth; for the eggshell crack does not let the vapor weigh down the mouth, and it is good medicine along with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times an arrow or bone lodges in the throat or somewhere else; therefore, you must draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with the whole instrument, so that you see the thing move; and if it does not open and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps this will loosen the thing through vomiting. Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of cotton, or a radish root, or one morsel of dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will stick, and then you will draw it out; and if it does not come out from what we have said, take one instrument made of wood in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be curved at the head so that it can enter more easily into the throat, and lift the head high; watch that you do not touch the epiglottis, that nothing harms it or push the bone inside; it is better if the patient pushes the instrument, because he can move it or the thing is air; if he pushes down, or pulls it all the way out, the instrument should be pulled out equally until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	the saliva from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Sometimes medicine is the saliva, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look in the throat of the patient towards the sun, since you press his tongue with the instrument that I told you. And if you see the saliva, take a small pair of scissors or fine pliers that are suitable for this purpose. If it is not suitable, take a thread and insert it into the mouth of the patient, then insert the end of the thread into a heated iron and do this repeatedly. Dye the patient with cold water throughout the day. Then take a full ounce of cold water, open his mouth, pour it in so that he can swallow it, and move it with your hand frequently; and as soon as the saliva feels the cold water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it does not fall as we have said, subdue the patient with asafetida, at the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will persist. The method of the fumigation is that you take one pot or it has charcoal inside, and cover it with a perforated cloth in the middle, and put the head of the instrument in it; then pour your fumigation, and make the patient hold the tip of the cane in their mouth, and close the mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but comes only up to the nostrils; and the nostrils will now persist, and if it does not fall, resume the fumigation many times; let the patient endure thirst, and eat salty and sour things, and drink no water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out under this management.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument for treating the nostrils is like curved tweezers to enter the throat; and resemble the beak of a syringe, and it should have abrasive limestone so that what it takes, it cannot release; here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
