Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Many abscesses resemble each other, according to what follows later in this book, and they differ in perforation and cutting; and it is in .ij. ways that one of them resembles itself and is due to moisture. And the second way is for the joints where they are in the body. because abscesses on the head are different than those on the foundation, and abscesses on the shoulder joint are different from those coming at jointures, and each one should have its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if abscesses should not be perforated until the boil is ripe according to its completion; and if there are such that it must be perforated when they become hard, and do not die according to their completion, as boils coming at jointures. Because boils coming at jointures, if left until they are covered over, there may be corruption of the ligament and nerve of the joint, causing contraction in the limb. Or if the abscess is from the main member, and you delay the perforation until it is ripe, this will harm the main member; or if it is from the foundation, if you perforate too soon when it is not yet ripe; and you should not perforate a hard abscess without digestion completed, except for one that is from the foundation, which could burst open, and become long inside, and a fistula forms; and it may not heal within a long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time of perforation of the abscess that is ripe according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the subsiding of the fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the loosening and shrinking of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the perforation sit on a lower place nearer to the abscess, and where it has opened; and the perforation should be along the body length, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, in joints, nerves, arteries, and in all equal places where there is no hair growth.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	1. When it strikes (affects), do so according to that member. And when an abscess is in the charred flesh, it is better to leave the perforation until it is confirmed in complete digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it beforehand, the body will be filled with much pus; and possibly harden the lips and deepen the wound. And for any abscess that are pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the limb requires. 2. It is necessary that you bring small perforations, small wounds; and large perforations, large wounds, and many cuts according to the resemblance of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where it is necessary to cover the wound, and bandage; when it has become as thin as cloth, and is swollen, it is necessary to do as with babies: and for those that are cut into four angles, and for those whose wound is coped like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses from wounds; and for such wounds where a round incision is made, and other similar cuts and bandages.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no head (no pus), like a superficial abscess, it is necessary that you pierce it fully; and when the abscess is large and it has collected much pus, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but draw out a part; then stop up the abscess until the next day, then draw nothing out of place; do this many times gradually, until the pus comes out entirely. This should be done carefully, especially if the patient is weak, or a woman bearing a child, or small children, or old men who are decrepit. The pus sometimes jumps out with the discharge, possibly killing the patient, and you must avoid this danger. Therefore, avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a large opening, bring linen or old cotton threads; and if it is a large abscess and there is much pus, it is necessary that you stuff in each a thread so that they meet; and if you have cut into the skin of the abscess and shaved it around, it is necessary to fill with old cotton or wool of linen without moisture, and bind until the third day; then remove it, and heal it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding occurs during your work, bring cold water and salt, and wet one cloth, and place it on the wound repeatedly.  And if the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter, and the limb or abscess is very nerve-racked, you must put hot tents and damp cloths over it; and if it is summer, and the limb is fleshy, you must put damp cloths over it with cold water and oil, or cold water and oil, until the third day, as we have said; and then lance the abscess and drain it, and treat it, as necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	This must be known universally in wound treatments: now I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	1. For the small abscesses that come in the head, there are ways known to us, such as those enclosed in linen, just like a gourd's knot and it has many resemblances. Some of them have fat with moisture, as pulses; and there are some hard and rocky ones at the base, and there is no doubt that the arteries do not oppose. And the operations of the neck are such that you should test everything. For what is called "entromissoire" determines the shape that follows, what it contains. If it contains moisture, they should be done above the long way. And when the moisture is emptied, scrape skin without leaving any remaining, as it returns again if something is left; then put cotton in Egyptian ointment, if available; otherwise, water and oil, and use it on the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who remain overnight will recover. And on the second day, repeat the cotton as before, on the third day, as long as you know that it does not remain overnight; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed. If the abscess is full of fat, press according to this form, along the length; and pour your eyes, and scrape from all sides, and apply your entire care for draining it where it lies; and if the arteries oppose you, do what I told you earlier. And similarly do with the hard abscess, and treat and cure as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And the cutting on the hard and moist abscess is lighter, for they have little blood. And if any of these abscesses or head has no moisture, and among them was one abscess that I pressed or head of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a quartz stone, rough and white, and could not break; and if you had cut any of it, you would have made a wound as deep as a quartz. In other abscesses coming from the heads, namely those that come on the heads of children and at the roots of the ears, they should be opened every day depending on the situation, to allow pus to escape; and treat them as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofulas
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Often this abscess appears at the neck, under the chin, and in groins, and sometimes it appears elsewhere on the body, and they are very large, and they are joined together. And each scrofula is specifically within its rib cage, as the abscess of the neck and the aposteme of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are numerous. There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that are malignant and do not want to obey health. Therefore, when you see a good position in the patient and resembles the color of the body, and is silent from all sides and is not swollen around the neck or the artery or the duct, and is not deep; then you should cut it open from above, and peel off each part, and put the two edges of the knife close to the incisions, if necessary, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and pull it gently and carefully, and ensure that you do not cover the nerve or the vein, and do not be too aggressive with the spatula or lance, so that the hand does not slip, and do not look too far ahead, so as not to cover what should not be covered.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or the artery and it does not let you pass, put vitriol powder in the wound, or some powders that stop bleeding, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are calmed and the wound softens and begins to purify. And when the pus is drained, return to your work as long as you complete it; then look for your guide if there remain small scrofulas in the root of the scrofula, cut them off and clean them up. And if there is a large scrofula in the root of the scrofula, do not cut that scrofula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it drop through; then use old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you excise the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you close the two lips of the wound and sew them now, as there should be no remaining superfluity due to the largeness of the scrofula. It is necessary that you understand to cover the root and draw pus, and sew as we have said. Those scrofulas with superfluity, pierce there where it has matured; and pierce in such a way as the one mentioned before, depending on it, then introduce tweezers with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, apply ointment-enriched charcoal until it heals.
de squinance	The patient should lie on his back, with the affected leg raised and supported by a cushion or similar object. Then, using a sharp instrument, make an incision from the groin to the knee, following the natural creases of the thigh. This incision should be wide enough to expose the underlying tissues but not so deep as to injure the femoral artery or veins. After making the incision, carefully remove any necrotic tissue, pus, and other debris from the wound. Once the wound is clean, apply ointment-enriched charcoal to promote healing.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the shape of the throat; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinting (squinance), the incision of the throat called "epiglote" should be opened; and it should not be helped by these [people], because all the veins and the passageway for the sickness are at those who have an abscess hot in the mouth, or in the throat or in two mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the sickness is in the passageway of the throat, it should be covered to avoid the danger of strangulation.   (When the sickness is located in the passageway of the throat, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to prevent strangulation.)
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, it should be cut below four circles or four small slits through the center, between the four circles, or according to the size of the slit, not in the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	and if the patient is susceptible to the incision of the epiglottis, there should be no cartilage, and the veins are long in length for this.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the master is afraid, then it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to its entire length, and cuts open the neck until it reaches the chin; and removes the veins containing blood, if you see anything, and then severs the trachea as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	And it is demonstrated by the section of the river of the chin that jumps due to the fractured jaw and by the lack of voice;
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	Leave the wound open a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which there is doubt about strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound with care and sew up the entire area against the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce healing, until it heals.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Zahrawi says not to do this until the throat is completely stopped up and the patient has been judged dead, and then let the bird fly away.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then press on the epiglottis because the patient cannot cough, and they breathe through the wound, and in this way they are kept from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	and the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the badness of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to sew up the wound and heal, until it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a young girl took one knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the windpipe.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to heal her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I found the wound and saw the blood coming out of it, and knew that she did not have any vein or conduit except for her throat, and the wind was going through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I hurried up, sewed the wound, and healed it until it was cured.   Si com li malaide avoit dit, il n’avoit aucune voine ne conduit qui issi fust mort.
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	And it did not happen to the maiden except that her voice was hoarse, and afterwards she returned to her position.
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	Therefore I say that in the condition of the epiglottis one should not have fear.
de la grosse gorge	from the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	This abscess is called "throat hernia" and it is a large abscess of a greenish color, and it is common in women.
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	And it is according to .ij. [two] ways: nature, and accidents; where nature has no instrument.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents are according to .ij. [two] ways, where one is similar to fatty tissue and the other way is similar to abscess which comes from us due to arteries.
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	and there is fear, and it should not be worked on without force except in the one that is small, and [it] proves and searches at all the entrance.
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it similar to fatty tissue and it does not open in any vein, if you press it, as one presses the nose, and draw it completely, if there is any;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And carefully examine it entirely, and treat it as appropriate, until it is perfectly healthy.
des nous	We have found that... (Incomplete sentence due to missing text)
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways of ours are there, which I will describe all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And it is necessary that I say all the differences that exist between a notch and an incision.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is heat and fever lasting, until the boils have passed and the porridge is complete; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With the newborn there is no heat, fever, or pain, and it contains one bladder, which is its own sac and is of the same color as the body, and begins like a blister and becomes large.
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they are according to two kinds: greasy or moist, and much of their color is as I said in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the cure of the newt, that you examine and test first all the instrument which is called "entromissoire", according to its form or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	The manner of the incision for abscesses is that you take or the moister place which you find in the abscess, and turn your thumb little by little, until you feel that the instrument has pierced through, then according to the size of the abscess.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then pull the entromissoire (the instrument), and take care that it does not fly out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	If moisture runs out of the wound, make it have the same color as I have said for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	and if after the incision no moisture comes out, knowing it is fatty, then make a cross incision, take hold of it with the forceps, peel it slightly from both sides and guard the coat where it lies so that you pull it safely with the suture;
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	and if you cannot pull it out safely, pull it out in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	If there remains nothing, the nose repeatedly returns many times;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it remains a little and does not bother you, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, hold the wound tight, place warm things on the abscess to alleviate the pain, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if the nose is large, you should cut two lips from the wound, and treat it with whatever heals flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against you or otherwise is opposed to you, or if you hasten and employ the leech of vitriol crushed, let it lie for 2 or 3 days until the wound heals, and let the boil of blood rest; then return to cover what has remained unhealed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of incising instruments, and they are of four kinds: large, medium, and small; and if there are four squares which are called 'albaret', and one which is called 'breb', and of three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle the abscesses with fistula.
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	and they are similar to the needles with which witches are sewn, and they are of citron wood, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable, and they are more experienced in black plank for encircling the swellings of fistula.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the wound.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the ulcers are much alike, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if an ulcer has two bumps in four ways as well;
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And if an ulcer has four bumps, it is also of four kinds; and if an ulcer has two bumps and one without a bump, they are all necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of these [bones] which are being cut is sharp, and those who do not cut it from one side, only from part, as we scrape the nerves, for this reason that the vein or nerve is not struck.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these intrusions [arrows] are the splinters returned in bandages, so that the patient does not pierce himself at the opening of the abscess.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	and they are of four kinds: large, small, and medium-sized, as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	And one should not use it [the cautery] elsewhere except in charnu, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar places;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And at times, another small instrument resembling a set of tourniquets is used, shaped like this, to draw blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed at times on the place where wounds heal quickly from veins and arteries, and sometimes round in this large shape.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	At times, the breasts of some men swell when they begin to rot, so that they resemble women's breasts.
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	And they remain swollen and inflamed, and whoever wishes to cure them, it must be done according to this form of the following line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape off the fat, and apply medication to the wound with soothing char, then close the lips of the wound together with stitches, and let it heal until it is healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	and if the limb bends downwards, and is deformed due to its large size as it often happens with women, then divide it into two pieces above by two similar incisions;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	With this, one should hold the other at the end of each, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line 'b' up to line 'g'.
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape the skin that is between the two lips (of the wound), remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitching and powders, and whatever is necessary in the treatment, until it heals.
et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healed or the incision is not completely made because the patient does not want to rest or due to bleeding, then you must fill the wound with cotton moistened in corrosive oil.
et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	And let it heal as it consumes the remaining flesh and fat, then cure it until it is healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	From abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the buttocks are handled as hard scrofulas where there are coats and if it contains moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those containing moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b up to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the boil that is in the abscess is emptied, use old cotton on the wound and leave it until another day, then remove all the cotton, and apply ointment afterwards until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess resembles scrofula, cut it as we have said in the incisions of scrofula, and if the wound boils again, apply a cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the artery is ruptured and the skin closed over it, it often leads to abscesses, and the same thing happens with an opened vein and abscess;
et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont;	and if one knows it by this sign, then the abscesses are long in length;
et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens .i. estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans;	and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels tight; and when it is for the vein, it appears rounded in appearance;
et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	It is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is under the armpits and groins and around the neck and in other places where it is large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc;	The iron cure must be avoided, and so must the one at the head. In the case of inflammation of an artery, cut through the skin from above.
puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte;	Then cut open the belly along the usual incision, and carefully separate the artery from the linen, leaving it exposed.
puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en .ij. leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des .ij. arteres qui sont en temples;	Then insert an awl beneath it, and make it pierce to the other side, and hold the artery with a double thread in 2 inches, as I have shown you in the extraction of the 2 arteries that are in the temples.
puis point le leu qui est entre les .ij. liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme;	Then push the area between the 2 joints with an instrument until it bursts open and the abscesses are separated.
puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient;	Then apply the cure of beechwood bark as long as the joint cries out.
puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then treat this [injury] with ointment, until it is healed.
et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir,	and if the abscess is due to the opening of the vein, then you must sign your hand with it all over the skin.
puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait .i. fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit;	then insert the needle under the skin that you hold with your hand, and make it go through, and have one double thread on it, so that you draw it from the other side.
puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de .ij. pars as .ij. chiés dou fil;	then tie the abscess as I told you, or sew one of the two parts to each of the two eyes with thread.
et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout .i. fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en .iiij. leus;	And if you doubt that the thread isn't inserted, push another needle through one of the threads beneath the abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pull the threads in four lengths;
puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez;	then cut away the abscess until the excess is removed, then cut away the curdled and leave that which is bound;
puis met sus .i. drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then put a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil on top, then apply treatments with bandages and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses from nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As in the artery and vein come abscesses, so do abscesses of nerves when they are wounded or by excessive labor, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est .i. grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor;	This happens more often in the shoulder and the arm, and all joints where there are connections, which is called serious abscesses, and its color resembles the body's color, and it feels pain in various positions.
et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur;	and when it is pressed firmly, the patient feels pain, but not throughout the body, but only under the skin.
et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction;	And it should be bound tightly from all sides, and neither go forward nor backward, neither above nor below, and he who is in the joints should not be covered with iron: perhaps there would be contraction.
et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And he who is at the head or forehead, scrape the skin with a spatula.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine;	If the abscess is small, take tweezers and strike its root.
et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is large, support it at the neck, and peel off the skin, then the bone and close the wound with stitches, and let it heal until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	hanging large growths
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans;	Sometimes happens in bellies and not elsewhere, and it is a disease called "fungus" because of its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has subtle roots, and large heads; there are small ones and very large ones.
et je vis .i. home qui en avoit .ij. ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	and I saw one man who had two bellies that resembled mushrooms more than anything else, and there was no difference between them, and they were white, and had a fine root, and were cut open, and ran continuously with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un .xviij. onces pesant, et en l’autre .vj. З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine;	I found and weighed one at 16 ounces, and the other at 7 ounces, and in the incision it is important to note that if the patient is moist and the color of the artery is pale and moist with a subtle root.
si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu. Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer;	If the wound is large, and in your presence the fire cautery is required. For there are often excessive bleeding during the cutting process, and if blood escapes without cauterization, then hasten to cauterize.
et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent .i. fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse .ij. jors;	and if you see the patient frightened and afraid of the incision with iron, take one thread made well, tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for 2 days.
et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet,	And then hold it (the shoulder), and not stop pulling on the cord of the pulley until it dislocates the joint, and you feel work being done; and if the roots are thick, be cautious about pulling too much from the belly, but you can certainly pull half of it.
puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Then burn (the shoulder) so it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to pull on the cord that is of a dark color, weak sensation, and poor sight.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an enlarged abscess, and I will come to the treatment of scrofula afterwards.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the buttock (or anus) is open/exposed
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit;	If the appearance of the buttock (or anus) comes from a wound or fissure due to cautery, and is on the abdomen and in some of the buttocks, as happens in other cases, or bleeding from veins or arteries, according to what is before, or diarrhea;
et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	And if it is through the fissure of the anus and the opening of the bowels, its appearance resembles the color of the abscess, and it causes little pain, and has an open wound with various discharge.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when it is pressed with the fingers if it shrinks back, and then returns, and possibly if it is hardened, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and by great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit;	If it is due to moisture, it is an easy thing, and opens readily when you press it with your hand, do not constrain it; if it is due to blood, it opens by these signs: the abscesses are large and hard, and they are pierced according to a quantity.
et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	and if it is due to gas, it yields easily to the touch, and the procedure is that you observe whether its appearance is due to blood from the artery or vein, or gas.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure. Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	It is necessary that you leave it (the patient) to heal. For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, due to the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude;	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or the belly, you must command the patient to strain his anals, and be stretched out straight, then press all around the abscess.
puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains,	then command him to press gently with your hands,
puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile,	Then go around the joint that you have signed with the spatula.
puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine;	Then spread the half of the abscess above to all the great uncine.
puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz;	Then tie it tightly with a strong thread or a cord of strong silk, and bind the nails to the limb.
puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine;	Then work half of the abscess extended over the ligament, and insert your finger, and search for the intestine.
se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre;	If you find it attached to the ligament, dislocate it, and push the intestine out of the abdomen.
et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit;	and if you find the bowel, take hold of it at its root, and cut off the excess.
et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren .ij. aguilles, et i boute .ij. fors filz, et boute les .ij. aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier;	and if the arteries or veins are obstructed, go carefully around it, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two thin wires through them, and place the two needles in a cross shape around what you have made pierced.
puis estrain l’aposteme en .iiij. leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi;	Then press the abscess for four leagues above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place as it is, and cut the dead flesh by itself.
ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit;	When it becomes subtle and can be pierced, then treat as necessary, and cover the abscess as we have said.
et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then treat the area as necessary, and stitch up the wound.
dou chancre	two boils
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We said in the previous division the resemblances of boils and how one should treat them with medicine, and how to avoid the iron cure; and we say that a boil starts in the groin, and great caution is required in its treatment, and the ancients said that when boils are in a place where it can be shaved as in boils that are on the breasts or in the thighs, and in similar places, one should remove them entirely at their beginning; and when they are large and old, it should not be approached because I never knew anyone to heal it; nor has anyone healed it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when in a place where it can be removed as we have said, is that you purge the patient once with black bile; then make him urinate if he has manifest fullness, then cut the patient one boin (a small knife) to perform the operation; then throw down your oncines (bandages or poultices) or boil, and shave off all the hair from all parts, and remove all the flesh without leaving anything; and let the blood flow freely, and be careful to anoint the place with your hand or something, and if the discharge of blood opposes the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize it until the blood is coagulated; then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Of hydropisy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces .ij. semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer:	We have already mentioned in the division the similarities of hydropisy and in what way water collection is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is made with medicine and the one that is cured with iron: only these two similarities are to be treated; iron should not be used for these .ij. similarities, namely tympanites and yposarche, as it is a fatal thing; therefore, when treating this hydropisy-like condition which is called "eclites" with medicine, and the cure does not help, examine whether the patient is weak or has another disease besides hydropisy, such as dropsy of the belly and similar things; if there is no iron to be used, because there is doubt; but if you see the patient with great strength, who has only hydropisy and does not have any other disease, and he is neither too young nor too old, then work in this way:
lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme: Et soit trenchans de .ij. pars. a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier;	Lay the patient down straight on your hands, and the attendant presses the abdomen towards the lowest part of the side, then take the curved spatula as shown in this form: It should be sharp at two ends. And it should not be so pointed that it can reach the intestine when inserted, nor can it be blunted;
puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude .iij. dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude .iij. dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu;	Then look to see if the urine is directed towards the intestines: if so, you must cut under the buttocks three inches straight up over the anus; and if the urine is due to liver disease, make the incision to the left of the buttocks three inches; and if it's due to stone, make it to the right, and it should not be done with the patient lying on the incision, so that excess fluids do not flow to the weak area.
puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme: Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz .i. petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, .iij. pertus; et .ij. d’autre part, et .i. d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Then pierce the skin with an instrument, push and pull your hand until you reach the bladder, just as when peeling fruit to the thickness of a nail or more; then pierce the bladder so that the spatula comes to the watery place, which is its location, then withdraw it, and bring out this tool in the form described here: It resembles a thin silver chain, made of light iron or brass, with one small hole at its base; and it has four holes on one side, two on another, and one on the other; and the head is shaped like a feather, and that's the shape of the incision where scribes cut the quill:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort;	On the head above is the esophagus, so when the instrument comes to the water, then hold it up now on the instrument; empty the lower part or one-third, because if you empty more than necessary in that hour, perhaps the patient may die due to the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he may fall down, or approach death.
mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit;	but empty according to the amount of its power, and according to what the condition of the patient and his pulse indicate; then draw out the instrument and stop the water, and it is now held back for the caution that stops the bleeding which is above the siphon, as I have spoken about, that you perforate in this manner; then repeat the instrument the next day if you see the patient suffering from the water, and draw out a small amount of water.
fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue. Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	Do this every day and be careful not to keep the water for too long but just a little. And if you have doubts about the patient, and you leave him with much water, cure him with sepulture or hot sand, and by much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and anoint with wine; and cure him with drying medicines until he is well, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after the extraction of the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Of stopping the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu. Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout .i. spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme: puis met ou pertus .i. clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi .iij. jors ou iiij. et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	At no time are born children who do not have foreskins on their penis, or the foreskin is small or out of place. If necessary, it must be circumcised immediately with a very thin spatula according to this form: then place a fine piece of cloth under the foreskin and hold and keep it in place for 2 to 4 days until it wants to urinate, at which point the cloth should be removed, and urine passed, and then the foreskin is placed back; and by chance, there should be no problem, because the urine that comes out does not leave the opening closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera. Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	If the foreskin is small, it should be treated with a piece of cloth as we have said, so that it expands. Those who do not have a foreskin at its place are eunuchs because no one is born with the foreskin on the head of the penis; therefore, they cannot urinate before lifting their penis, and they cannot enjoy sex because matter cannot come to the opening, which is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the method of work is that the patient lies supine on their back, their head should be slightly elevated and the neck similarly to the thickness of a feather, so that the patient's chin touches their chest, as required; and guard against bleeding which occurs frequently, and if it happens, stop it by pressing the area that is bleeding, and treat the wound until it heals.
des pustules de la verge	of boils on the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often this albathion appears in the penis, and it is an appearance of ugly genital warts; and there are both malignant and non-malignant ones; you should take them one by one with a subtle instrument, cut and clean all of them, then put cotton moistened in Egyptian ointment on top; then treat it with the ointment diafinicon until it heals.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere. Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer. Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the elbow is diseased with a putrid color and swollen, you must apply cautery. When you have heated it, and if the elbow joint is inside the arm and has both parts within the flesh and outside, you must first remove the diseased part that is inside; when it is seared, you should treat the outside. For when you are treating it together, the limb of the arm is not assured that it will not be pierced, and it becomes darker and corrupted in the arm and joint; therefore, you must scrape off all that is black and corrupted, then put it on a plaster of honey and flour made from the peel of pommegranate rind and various herbs, and treat it with other remedies until it becomes healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme: Li cauteres si aide as .ij. dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a .i. estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars;	And when bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cautery according to this form: The cauterizer should aid in two positions at once: namely, for bleeding and corruption; and if the limb of the arm is corrupted and retracted, you must bring or cause a cord made of yew wood from the arm, and make the patient urinate; when the hair is loose at the tip of the arm where it occurs in those who have not been circumcised, or it occurs due to injury or abscess, then you must shave it with one instrument, until the ligaments are loosened, and the limb of the arm is freed from all sides.
et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a .i. spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre .ij., et i met .i. subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if it is a grave matter to speak of this, you must shave it with one razor blade, a little bit of hair from the tip of the arm and the flesh; then squeeze it out very gently between 1 and 2 hours, and place 1 linen cloth dampened with cold vinegar on it so that it does not become inflamed immediately.
de la circoncision	Of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not just a cutting like other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our own will and specifically on infants, it is necessary to make the best and easiest work for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children, for they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have wanted the greater part of masters and saints who perform circumcision around day one, and for forces, and in all cases with a novacule; however, it is feared because there are two layers, and by chance if one above is cut, the one below may remain.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now it should be covered, and the pain is doubled; and at the amputation which is deep in the limb, there is no assurance of the point of the member; and during the amputation of the nail, by chance the iron may slip, and spoil the work, and many times it is not necessary for amputation, and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	In amputation which is done with the forceps, I have found the advantage of the experiment, because the forceps cut evenly both above and below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	For when you press your hand, you cut evenly all the time; but that the thread should be tightly wrapped around the skin; and follow the method of the first work, so you make the child think that you will not tie the thread only around the rod, but rather let it be free in all the ways that you can.
puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz .i. poc a .i. autre liien; et la tien as .ij. dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les .ij. liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge;	Then make it be between your hands straight, and reapply the forces between your hands or under your feet so that the infant does not see, nor any of the instruments; then push your hand to the shaft and blow or scream, and draw it up as far as the head of the shaft is in; then clean it well of the filth that has accumulated there, then tie the joint with a double thread, then tie it under one peg to another link; and hold it with two fingers by the second knot, and press between the links, then quickly pull the core upwards and draw the head of the shaft;
puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre .i. drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Leave the pus to flow out drop by drop, for it is the poison; and put powder on top and above the powder, one cloth glued with a mixture of cooked egg white steeped in rose water, combined with fresh rose oil, let it remain until the next day, and treat it with another remedy until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces for cleansing is as follows: the two heads should be tender and sharp, and their heads should be as large as a hand equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error in the incision of the womb is when the bowels inside are cut; therefore it is necessary that you stretch it with your nail so that the opening resembles an abscess, and then press it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your nail, grasp it with forceps, and then press.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they exceed three days, and what is beneath the scrotum swells, leave it until the abscesses are appeased and gently incise the skin; then press as you can move it, and be careful of the part of the scrotum, which will not harm it.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, treat the limb with things buried in a wound with the powder we have mentioned or how to treat wounds with powders, and if you press too hard, it will go upwards, but it will not harm; therefore, treat it as we have said until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	Retention of urine is due to obstruction by a stone, or congealed blood, or pus, or frozen urine, or similar things, as we have said in the division;
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And if the urine is not released and you see that retention occurs due to the stone lodged in or neck of the bladder, it is necessary for the patient to be bent on his knees; and his feet should be placed on a chair or the back, and he should extend his abdomen from above the lower back, and restrain the patient as much as possible; then pressure is applied to the neck of the bladder to push out the stone, so that the urine is released.
et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	And if it does not occur as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, you must administer extraction with all the instruments called "syringe," of which this is the form: it should be made of thin delicate silver tube, like the quill of a bird; and the tip of one and a half palm length, and should be fine at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren .i. fil double, et lie au chief .i. poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus .i. siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede;	The way to extract urine is that you take a double thread, tie one end of it to a piece of wool or cotton, and stick the end of the thread into the syringe; then tie the excess wool and stick the end of the syringe, then oil or butter and egg white should be applied to the syringe, and make the patient sit on a chair, and rub the bladder and penis with moist oil of olive and cold water.
puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine;	Then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then bend the penis upward towards the anus; then insert the syringe in front up to the bladder, and make the patient feel the urine coming up to the empty place, and this is not done according to this order unless because the conductor guides where it goes is twisted; then the thread is attached to all the wool pieces, and the urine follows the wool, then remove the thread, and correct the urine;
et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And fill the syringe until the bladder is empty, and the patient urinates.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scorching or blood comes into the bladder, or pus is collected there, and you see it distill liquids and medications, do with all the equipment that is called "clepsydra", and this is its form:
Elle est close, et si a .iij. pertus: .ij. d’une part, et .i. d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est;	It is closed, and has three openings: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the limbs join by which the medicine can be applied so that it stops the flow of moisture well, if it can draw out the moisture, and push when necessary;
et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira;	and when you wish to throw your medicines into the bladder, place the head of the cupping glass in the moisture, and draw out the drawing that is within; if you draw out the moisture with the cup, and then forcefully push back the drawing inside, the moisture will enter the glass, and come to the bladder immediately, so that the patient will feel it;
