et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	and this is the form of the subtle enema by which one administers an enema to the bladder:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a .i. sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les .ij. seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe .i. poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie;	And it is made of silver or iron, and the head [the dislocated part] is raised higher; below it there is one breast or the ligaments fall; then take a sheep's bladder and fill it with the moisture you use to cleanse the bladder, then tie it between two breasts using a good thread doubled, and heat one end of the moistened bladder over the fire; then insert the head of the clistere [a tool used for introducing liquids into the body] into the urethra, then hold your hand above the bladder with all the moisture coming towards it, until the patient feels that the moisturized bladder has reached the bladder.
et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai .i. cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute .i. fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble .i. dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And if you do not have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make one circle, and pierce it roundly all around; then insert a strong thread into these holes, then assemble the circle like you would assemble a syringe, and put inside that which you use for oil, moisture, and water, and seal it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division about the ways of stone, and extraction combined with medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone embedded in the flesh, and all the signs, and when to operate on it by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the member; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	The stone embedded in the bladder often happens to children, and this is a sign that the urine jumps from the bladder like urine in its subtlety; it opens a hole, and makes the patient's member swell, and he pees many times, then strangles himself; and many foundations occur due to these jumps; and it is easy for children to heal until they are 4 years old, but it is severe in adults, and it is in the middle range for those who are between youth and old age; and it is easier to cure those who have large stones than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	And when we come to the cure, first it is necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines. Because it sometimes obstructs the search for the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche ded ens;	Then take the patient by the feet, turn them and move them downwards, until the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and never move it up again; then make him sit between your hands, his hands below his thighs, so that the bladder is completely inclined downwards; then press and touch it with [something].
se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere. Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut it above the stone. And if it does not fall with the touch, wet your index finger of the left hand, if the patient is an infant, or your thumb, if the patient is a young adult; and push it into its foundation, and squeeze the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, move it to the neck of the bladder; then press down on it, and push it towards the place where you intend to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend his right hand upwards, and with his left hand remove the skin that is below the scrotum in the part where the cutting is done; then insert the spatula covering it, which is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans;	And it should be between the coccyx and the pelvis, not in the middle but on the left side of the lower back; and it should be straight across the stone, and your hands should be close to or at the base, and the incision should be wide at the top and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large;
par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	In case the hands pressing down at the base jump due to strain, know that there is this stone or it has angles and edges: it is necessary to be careful; if it is soft like a plum and round, where the opening is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li .i. estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge .i. poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole;	For the one who has angles and edges, make the incision larger; if it does not open, you must tighten with pliers like a chisel at the tip to press the stone so it does not slip away; or you can use a small curved instrument at the tip to press down on it. And if you cannot deceive it in this way, make a small hole and cut through the stone without taking it out, then tighten with vitriol;
et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie. Car .ij. choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces;	1. And if there is more than one arrow, push the largest one first into the bladder's neck, then strike it, pull it out, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are any more. And if it is very large, it must be cut open, and make a larger incision.
et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus .i. drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	Once you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it together, then place one damp, oil-soaked cloth on top of it or oil and cold rose water and cold water to cool the abscess; then make the patient lie down on his neck, and do not loosen the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you loosen the bandage, clean the wound very well with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of defyacinicon and basilicon until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit;	And if an abscess comes in the wound and corrosion occurs, and blood congeals in the bladder, keeping the urine back, which is known to occur without pain with the urine: therefore press your hand on the wound, draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and cause its rupture;
puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les .ij. cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	lift the wound from water and pus and dressings, and help in all ways you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that you tie up the two legs of the patient, and gather the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	If the stone is small and it is conducted by the urine and fixed inside, and the urine cannot be expelled; you should cure it with what I say next, namely, to cut many times, and excuse yourself from the cutting by this cure. I have already proven this thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron rod of this form and sharpened at four angles on one point:
puis pren .i. fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides;	then take one thread and twist it around the rod under the stone so that it cannot return into the bladder; then push the rod gently into the rod until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod slightly in the stone bit by bit, as much as you can pierce the stone from the other side; if urine comes out immediately, press your hand on the part of the stone that is inside the rod. It will soon be broken, and pass with the urine, and the patient is healed.
et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie .i. fil desoz la piere et .i. autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les .ij. liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and if you cannot do that for any reason that prevents it, then tie one thread under the stone and another above, then push the rod towards the stone between the two threads, then pull it out, and untie the thread, and clean the congealed blood in the wound; and heal it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	Of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone appears in women, and if it ever occurs, it is a great grief for the woman, and it is forbidden for four reasons: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows herself well enough to be examined by mirrors, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman is deeper than the stone of a man, therefore it requires a more profound incision, causing great fear.
Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier .i. caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere;	And if you need assistance with this matter, then you must find a skilled midwife, and if you cannot find one, do not hesitate to call upon one chaste virgin; and present a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows some part of the art, and order her to perform whatever you command regarding the incision of the stone.
et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And pay close attention to whether the woman is a virgin; then you should insert your finger or probe and search for the stone; if you find it, confine it under your finger, and advise her to push with her hand where the patient is in pain, and press her left hand against the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite;	If you find it (the stone), you should make her push it gently from the entrance of the bladder towards the root of the thigh until it reaches the root; then strike on the stone at the root of the thigh near the middle of the vagina, where it is moved apart, and feel the stone in that area; do not move your finger above or below the stone, and cut it into pieces at the first small piece.
puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	Then push the root (of the stone) into the thigh, if you feel the stone, press the wound so that the stone can come out further, and know that there are many types of stones: small or large, rough or smooth, long or round, and those with grooves. Know their characteristics to determine the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre;	And if the wound opens up, apply powdered vitriol and hold it in place for an hour until the wound stops bleeding; then return to your work, while the stone remains hard, and have tools that I told you about for extracting the stone from a man to help you in your work.
et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If the wound is an artery that has been cut, place powder on it and bind with bandages, do not start again and leave the stone untouched and do not draw it out for fear of killing the patient; then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the heat of the blood has subsided and the swelling has decreased, return to your work while the stone remains hard.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Aqueous is not otherwise called an accumulation of moisture or white chyle, which is beneath the bladder, containing the egg; and it is called "chyle," and sometimes it is properly in the egg's membrane, if one thinks that it is another egg; and it is the skin of the bladder between the white chyle we have mentioned; and this does not happen except when there is an empty space.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the growth of this aqueous is due to weakness that comes from the bladder, and that matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus;	And sometimes there comes percussion on the head, and this moisture can have various colors: either it is yellowish declining, or without red, or black, or watery white, and this happens more often.
et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, .i. poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	and these are the signs to recognize this assembly, for if it is white as we have said, then it is an abscess, that is, long like an egg's figure, and does not open the head, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef;	and if there is moisture in the actual cloth, it is an abscess with part of an egg, and for this reason, they think that it is another egg.
et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	If moisture is between the skin and the white flesh (subcutaneous tissue), it can be felt easily; therefore, to know the color of the moisture, probe it thoroughly with the intruder, so that you can determine its form as described before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, judge what is inside through the intruder.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz;	When we cure it with iron (using a fire cautery), the patient should be purified as much as possible and his body should be filled. Then lay him on his back, on something slightly raised, and put many cloths underneath him;
puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des .ij. costelz dou keur des coions;	Then he should lie on his left side, and command the minister to be on his right, and extend the arm towards one of the two ribs of the chest.

puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a .i. large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue;	Then pierce the white part with one large hole and drain all the fluid, then put your thumbs, and stretch the white part upward; and do not touch the nipple but only the white part; strike everywhere or in pieces gently the rib of it if you don't strike it well, the fluid will return.
et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les .ij. leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the egg (fetus) jumps out of your work, reset it in its place when you have completed the procedure with the knife; then gather the two levers from the knees and stitch them together, then treat it as for other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	If the egg (fetus) is corrupted by another disease, then it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspended, fearing the release of blood; next, cut the cord entirely and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en .ij. parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont .ij. ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset;	And if the egg (fetus) is assembled in two parts joined together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part as you have done the first equally, next squeeze out the blood, and put linen soaked in rose oil on the wound.
et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les .ij. coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And place other moistened wool in vinegar and oil on it, and put two coins on top, and cover with double cloths, and tie it above all the band that is in this shape:
Puis pren .ij. drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les .ij. angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier;	Then take two cloths, and use moistened linen according to this pattern and assemble them in the loincloth strap, and one of the coins should be placed on the bottom up to the back, and the other at the hilt part; and the other coin on top of the two angles, and assemble the rest of the strap in the buckle of the loincloth.
et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes .i. cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers;	And sometimes this remedy is a cautery ramie in the size of an iron knife, and you should take one subtle cautery cutlery, and make the hide of the coins hot as we have said, so that the white pus that contains the water is exposed.

et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And if anything happens contrary (to what you expect), either an abscess forms or the flow of blood or something else, then treat what is happening contrary to you, according to what has been said before.

de l’aposteme des coions	From the abscess of the eye
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse;	Verify that in the section of this treatment many people are afraid with various dispositions, which is why it seems to me that one should leave it.

Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Then, many abscesses come from bodies or heads; this happens often.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion;	It is known by excessive sour and hot fluid spreading in the head, or due to injury.

de hernie carnouse	Of a carnous hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this remedy, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz;	And the ancients said that it is done in a manner similar to the remedy which includes a nail, in such a way that you tie the vessels, above the wound lightly below;
puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, insert the nail and heal the abscess of those who are opening, as long as the vessels leak; and heal it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres;	Sometimes rot comes in wounds, as we have said, and they are opened; no intestines should be removed from the openings, and if some are, it is little, and repair them every hour.
et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent;	Moreover, if it remains too long at this point, the wound or ulcer grows so much that the intestines come out.
et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert;	And this happens because of the swelling of the ulcer in wounds, as we have said, since it is extended, then softened and opened the flesh.
et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere:	And the cure is by cautery, as we have previously stated; and sometimes it is cured by iron in this manner:
et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de .iij. dois;	and the patient lies supine on his back between your hands, then strike the swelling along the rupture with a flatiron of three fingers width;
et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac;	and draw out the pus that is under the skin, then take the rod and put it on the swollen area of the sore;
et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les .ij. leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre;	and press firmly with the abdomen, then cut the two visible areas of the sore on top of the rod, and cut both;
puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines;	Then straighten the head (of the patient), and do not apply any oil or cover it with an egg nor extend the eye nor anything else, as I have told you in the treatment of the ramyke (abscess) of the intestines;
puis le cure par la cure des plaies. Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Then treat it with wound treatments. And when you apply threads, if he suffers from an abscess and treats the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The ointment is confined and has no appearance in the wound, and cauteries are made here and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	Of the softening of the skin around the eyes
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Often the skin around the eyes becomes soft in some men, because the glands within are softened and there is pus to see; and when it is observed that it needs to be cured, it is necessary to make the patient lie on his back, and to strike the softened skin with the natural skin; then bring together the two lips at a stitch, and if you see, sew the excess of the softened skin at three or four stitches firmly; then strike between the stitches, and let the cure be as for other wounds, until it is healed, and stitch the threads.
dou chastrement	When struck with a blow
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes. Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc .ij. manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.  En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.  Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a .i. cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	1. Know that castrations are condemned in our law, and I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the eyes answer when questioned about it and its cure; and the other, because we often need castration of certain animals to help us, such as a pig, a sheep, a goat and others. I therefore say that castrations are done in two ways: by attraction or by incision. In the method we do by attraction, we seize the animal in hot water until the genitals soften and swell; then we grasp it with our hand, keeping it pressed until it is put back and you no longer feel it.
des hermofrodites	The translation for "des hermofrodites" in this context would be "hermaphrodites". This term refers to individuals with both male and female sexual characteristics or reproductive organs. In medieval times, such individuals were often considered abnormal or even monstrous by some societies due to their ambiguous gender identity.
Hermofrodie est selonc .ij. manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les .ij. coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.  Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et .ij. coions.  Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	Hermaphrodites are of two types: in men, there is an opening between the two genitals as in the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair and sometimes urine from inside. And in women, it has something like a penis and two genitals. The treatment for men and women is to cut around the scrotum and heal them as with other wounds; but in the second case, for men who urinate through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the torture
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure. Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee». Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	The torture is a boil located on a natural part, which is too ugly to look at; and some women have as large a boil as a hand, and it is called a cure. It is necessary that you dye the surplus of the boil with your hand or onions, and gently strike it; do not go too deep so that blood does not come out, then heal it with another treatment until it becomes healthy again; and at another boil that arises from the mouth of the sore, use it, and perhaps jump out and resemble a cow, and for this reason they called it in ancient times "kowe disease". If you must strike it, as we have said about the boil, then heal it until it becomes healthy again.
de erratique	Of the eructation
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile. Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait. S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as .ij. leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes .ij. dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les .ij. leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder. Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte. Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.  Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez. Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	1. The erratic is when the nature of a woman is not discernible, or it is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to disease that comes about; or it is by false union, or from subtle or thick sperm, and it is complete in the marriage, or outside, wherever it may be; and they must conceive, give birth, and sometimes produce flowers; and their knowledge of this is through the observation of the belly. If the effusion appears imminent, whether at your hand or side, if it is subtle sperm, and it is near the two leves (levels?), hasten and act in this way: place your two index fingers together, and the woman should be on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two leves (levels?), so that the subtle sperm is rounded, and the effusion is stopped; then take wool, wet it in oil, and put it on the spot, and have the woman lie down at home every day, so that it does not heal. And if the sperm is hard and thick, you must cut it with a spatumile (spatula), shaped like a mirte leaf. If the effusion is of blood, stop it at the onyx (clitoris) and cut; have medicines to stop bleeding, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, along with much egg; then bring a wide plank bandage so that the wound does not heal; and in this way, it should be long-lasting, and bring a linen dry tent; then cure other wounds until it heals. And when in marriage, char nee (blood) comes, it must be covered in this manner, unless there is an abscess festered. For the abscess festered that is in the marriage, one should not touch to heal.
des emorroides	Emorroidal lesions
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation. Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer. Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer. Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai .i. emplaustre sus son dos. Et se il estainche, c’est boin. Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.  Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a .i. chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Emorroidal openings are exposures of veins, which without treatment usually occur; and when emorroidal openings become old, they swell; and as we have said in the division, their resemblances, signs, and cures have been explained. I will now tell you those that respond to treatment. I say that emorroids and the swelling, when they are fully formed in the anus, cannot be felt, unless they are treated with iron. Those at the opening of the anus can be felt, and these are those that can be cured. Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then attach the swelling to the tweezers, and cut off its roots. Then sprinkle medicinal powders on it, such as acacia powder and dragon's blood powder and incense and similar things; then press her feet against the opening for an hour, then immerse her in cold water. And when bleeding stops, place her in a decoction of sumac and grapefruit peel and hawthorn leaves and similar things, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and oil, and make one poultice on her back. If it itches, that is good. If not, fartether blisters on the back and near the nipples without piercing them; then take linen, wet it in juice of plantain or jujube tree leaves with old wine, and apply it to the area. And when the abscess rests, cure the area with ointment until it heals; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough crust, which should be covered as I have said for the swelling; and then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	abscesses in the anus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division. Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.  Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus .i. siege, et ait .ij. petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument. Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés .ij. jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.  Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come in the anus, such as boils, hard and painful abscesses, herpes, ulcers, fistulas, emorroids, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division. Therefore, it is necessary for me to tell you here about the hot abscess that comes in the anus, which is not one of the boils that are round; and if you want to know how to use iron, observe if the abscess is hard at the beginning of its appearance, filled with heat and fever, and turns red when touched. Then do not hurry to pierce it, but let it ripen until the pain subsides; and then place the patient on one seat, or two small seats where he can lean, and support his back and feet against the legs; and spread his thighs, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good rope; then direct the pus towards the right side, and bring out the tool for opening the anus, as follows: when you bring this tool, it is necessary that when you introduce it, it does not go in too far and does not hurt the patient; if the tool is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the anus with cloth, so that the tool does not hurt it; and it must be inserted with the cup of the tool on top, and tied. And when the abscess opens, and one massages it by hand, it should be covered with a linen cloth at the head, and with a spatula made of soft leather or waxed paper; and when the pus is emptied, it should be covered with tents moistened in rose oil or dry green oil; place the tent over the wound towards the back and over the anus and over the handle with clean, wet linen that has been boiled or macerated. Then treat it after two days with ointment as previously described until it heals; and sometimes the anus and the wound are lifted with water and honey, and then long root of lis or aristolochia root cooked in water is applied; then return to the ointment. And if the wound returns to the anus, it is necessary to avoid using iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment. Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	The midwife must first recognize the figure of natural childbirth and its signs when she sees the woman dilate in the lower part and desire to smell the air; then hasten for the infant to come forth; thus know that this childbirth is according to nature, and is born through the vagina, accompanied by a second one; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to press gently on the woman's belly so that the infant comes out quickly; for when it descends towards the head, the second one follows it, and the husband cleans himself of his superfluities with good purification; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes over its feet, or the body or the shoulders, or the hands, or on the belly, or on the back, and is turned by chance over its neck, and in other evil ways; therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skillful in these matters, and to avoid error and deception, and I will show you all the figures on how one should assist.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the infant comes out over its head naturally and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, make her sit on a saddle or have other women hold her; anoint her nature with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, then the midwife should insert a small spatula of this shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.Et se les .ij. mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus .i. siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	1. And split the second [birth canal], and strike its tip with its nail until the moisture which is within it comes out; and hold the woman's belly as the baby descends, and if it doesn't descend, you must plaster her with musk-based poultice of fenugreek with camomile oil; then make her take in deep breaths and vomit, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: this will now help the baby.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piez	3. Of the birth of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut;	When the baby comes out on its feet, you must push it upwards;
et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz;	And then turn the thigh bone by thigh bone, until they are even.
puis preigne .i. des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	Then take a piece and stretch the thigh bone by thigh bone.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi;	Can it jump up to the knees if commanded, and make it expel everything inside with a push?
si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If God wills, it will jump.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it is not as we have said, turn it bit by bit, until it is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Then it will be easily.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons dit, si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en .i. mortier;	And if it does not come as we have said, take muskroot of height, and oil from the sage plant, and melted resin, and grind all in one mortar.

de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the birth of the child on its knees

et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main;	And if it does not give birth [to a baby], make her sit on a seat or stool, then study the method of repositioning the hand.

de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Hold the baby by its neck and spread out your hands, then turn its face towards the back of its mother.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement;	The ball should hold [the baby's] hand, then gently pull and twist it [in a clockwise direction].
et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc;	And when it is even, place on top the muscle balm of high altitude and oil, as we have said, then instruct it to move slowly;
et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus .i. siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	Then, once you have done this, make her sit on a chair and instruct her to grab hold of herself; then make her vomit.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In this same way, you must follow it through to the end.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie;	When it comes to this method, you must continue the procedure until the moisture is drained by squeezing the instrument with your fingernail.
et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes;	And if the infant is placed on its face and neck, press down on the abdomen, so that it is not held back, and the infant dies.
puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois:	then push the child inside until you have put it as necessary, and command the woman to take care of herself once.
adonques si istra legierement.	gently pull (the child) out.
de l’issue des gemelz	from the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born often, and sometimes triplets or quadruplets; and this is not strange and rarely happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom;	Twins are rare and do not live long if you call them by name;
je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude;	I know that they are multiplied, and they are destroyed by the scribe who divides them, who is associated with death.
et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	And sometimes it occurs as naturally as one gives birth, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait;	If it comes forth laboriously, as the treatment has been described and let the balm be subtle, make it quickly and lightly as required.
et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And make it according to what is worth moving towards salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vj. ou .vij., ou plusors jusc’a .xv., et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious,	Sometimes they are formed in the womb, one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the sagely grown,

si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Then act according to what is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	Of a dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains;	When you cure the woman of a dead or unborn child, as I said in the division, and it does not come forth, and you are forced to work by hand;
si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort;	it is necessary that you know if the woman is of good virtue, and has no sickness or fear of death;
si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees;	The woman must lie on her back, with her head inclined downwards, and her legs raised.
et li ministre la teigne de .ij. pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant;	And the midwife should pull on both sides of the woman's belly, or tie her to the bed so that she is not treated in the delivery of the child.
puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges;	Then rub the mouth of the woman with moist oil mixed with musk and aloe and flax seed, then anoint the midwife's hands with these oils and these mixtures.
puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere .i. leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu,	Then push gently into the joint, then hold one joint where it pushes in until it can be moved.
et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief;	and prepare if the bone is dislocated upward towards its head.
si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez,	insert fingers in the joint or neck or mouth or palate or below the beard or wrist or near the sides.
et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes;	if the dislocation is at the feet, insert or press and apply pressure to the middle of the bones.
et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide;	And it is necessary that the onyx be held with the right hand, and place the concavity between its two hands of the left hand, and push gently with all his hand, and pierce the onyx in one of the positions we have mentioned, until it comes to an empty thing;
et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	And this is the shape of the onyx:
puis fiche encontre .i. autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz;	then pierce against one other onyx, or where you have it at hand, so that the extraction is even;
et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	And then equal it by moving it from one side to the other, so that it may move; and the joints should be set for holding it in place, as shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie;	And if there remains some part of it, the healer applies oil to some of his fingers and pushes into that part, drawing the other part.
et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains no part of it, put this joint or higher up and do so until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement,	If one hand comes before the other and cannot be returned by pulling,  \]
si covient que tu envoloupes sus .i. drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote;	If you need to turn something over, do it until it's all turned.

Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee,	And if the child's head is fat and narrow at the exit, or if it has a sharp collection of bone.

ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui;	You will go to the instrument called "almidach", from which the shape comes with the tools or chapter that follows this one.

Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman whose belly had been stillborn, then consulted with another on this matter, and revived the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in the armpit, and swelled so much that it opened, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal, and I thought for a long time, but could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong plaster of attraction, and afterwards, some bone came out, and after several days another one did.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled much, because the stomach has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.

et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	and keep the woman in this position for a long time, and then proceed with a little bit of pressure on the bone;

dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the husband to his place

Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis;	When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold in her urine, and then make her vomit with something bitter, and hold your hands at her mouth and nose.

de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac:	Many children are born who have not yet pierced their foundation, but it has been stopped by some subtle means.

This text suggests that the authors are discussing how to treat wounds and abscesses. They recommend using a wooden peg for certain types of injuries, and also suggest covering them with lard (pork fat) if they swell suddenly.

The phrase "de la fistule dou fondement" refers to treating this condition from its base.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des .ij. parties,	Bladder stones that come from beneath the foundation are nodular, and those that emerge from the foundation's side, or in the gap between two parts,   (Translation for line 1)

Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe. puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	then insert a tent of linen or wood if there is crookedness, as you know where the tent comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice,	If the patient feels it around the base, you must insert your finger.
se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans;	If it pierces the patient through, and it is discovered or you feel between your finger and the flesh, then know that it is penetrated.
si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	and it shall not be worked at all, for it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc;	One must know that one can heal some, but it happens little;
et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit;	and help is given to him, when one heats the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before;
et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu .ij. fois ou .iij., tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil;	and fill the entire thing in the fistula until it comes out from its base; and do this 2 or 3 times, as you know that these little charred things should be burned, which are similar to a bird's feather;
et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	And then heal the swollen tents with butter, until the heat subsides, then heal it with a healing ointment, warm and binding.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien. Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez;	If that heals, that's good. But if it cannot be healed otherwise,
et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur;	and if the tent enters in, and does not pierce to the depth where the foundation is, and between your hand and the tent put a thick covering of skin or cloth, and you see the fistula beneath that cover with care.
si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente;	If the edge of the fistula begins, push it forward toward the tent, and then apply the fire cautery until it reaches the tip of the tent.
et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	The tent will be released and cut; then take out the charred pieces that seem like a feather of a bird, and nothing remains.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the flesh wounds itself, cut between you and the wound; then cauterize it with fire or medicine ointment.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble .ij. bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor;	For the fire cauteries have two good qualities: burning of these charred pieces and stopping the flow of blood and drying up the moisture.
puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe;	Then, treat wet tent wounds with butter or crushed oatmeal until the flesh becomes soft and the charred part is submerged in it.
puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Then treat deep, hard, charred sores with dry, sharp instruments as the remedies are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it becomes healed and does not return again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the full depth and is removed from the body, push it down towards the foundation and examine it.   The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre .ij. est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des .iii. manieres:	If you feel the temptation and there is a thin cloth or leather or skin close to piercing it, there should be no escape but only a way of faith and hope through the administration of one of the three methods:
ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier;	or you cauterize it as we have said, or you plunge it to the hilt, or if there is pus, place a lance and cure it as before;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit;	and do not go too far in, covering the foundation's support, and let the exudations come out through it voluntarily;
puis le cure, si com nos avons dit;	then heal, as we have said;
par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé;	if by chance it becomes healthy, then you remove that covering and clean it when it is cut off at the base, either with a probe or another instrument pointed.
puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues;	then disinfect that charred flesh that is in the wound, as much as you can;
puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	then study to restore the wound and keep the fistula in the area away from the base: it will be easier for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus,	And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you bite the tent (or opening) into the fistula, and it is where it touches the foundation underneath the skin on top.
si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	Take a small hole pierced on the cheek in this manner:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	and push one thread of cord through it (the small hole), and push the tent into the fistula all the way to its end, along with the thread.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement;	If it is perforated at the foundation margin inside, then pull out the thread so that you can push your finger (or the foundation).
et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les .ij. chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse .i. jor ou .ij.;	And draw out the head with thread, and put together the two shoulders together, and hold one to the other, and leave it for 1 or 2 days;
et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent;	And hold it without moving, until the threads sew together these things that are between them, and bind;
puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	Then heal the wound when it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If there is no fistula, make it pierced in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep.  \[Fistula is a tube-like passage between two organs or through the skin.\]
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is not right to cover the fracture with a bandage immediately upon setting it, and then heal it as we have said, until it heals completely.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans;	The shape of the thorn-like splint used to make a fistula is very sharp at one end and cuts through.
et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	and on the other hand it is not blunt, so as not to cover what should not be covered, as you see here.
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc ij. manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc,	Emordices are of two kinds: they are within the foundation, as grain of resin, and if there are small or large ones, and on the outside blood is present.
et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor,	and if there is one or more, they are displaced from the foundation and at the head of the foundation; but those that are displaced have a little moisture,
et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors;	And still always or a little amount of citrus juice or a little blood, and have the color of the body;
et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz;	and the care of those who have it within the foundation, is that you command the patient to strain themselves to urinate in chambers, until the foundations subside, and the sons appear.
si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines;	if you hurry, and pierce it with tongs or hold it with your nail, then strike its roots.
et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a .i. drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot;	and if the tongs cannot hold them because of moisture, then take it with a cloth or cotton or a piece of gauze.
et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere;	And pull it to your arms, then strike it, and powder on top of some hot powders that are in place of the cautery;
ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, puis les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	or you cauterize it as stated or in the chapter on cauterization, then you treat it with other treatments until it is healed;
et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement;	and if the foundation cannot come out, clisterize the patient with a harsh and biting clyster to wash the affected area, so that it comes out openly;
cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere;	The patient should not prepare himself, and if his veins are forced from their foundation, it is a light cure.
et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	And you should grasp them with your nail or tweezers and strike them, then heal them as we have said, until they are healthy and fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren .i. fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les .ij. chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille,	You should apply the stitching in this manner: take a twisted thread, put it into a needle, then draw the thread above and pierce the needle from the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread below the needle.
et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse .i. por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	and if it is wide, make the stitches close, then knot the thread, pull out the needle, and do the same with all the others, leaving one for draining excess blood;
puis met sus le fondement .i. drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	Then place a soft cloth soaked in rose oil or cerot on the foundation, and place it there, and instruct the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then leave it until it stops draining, and when it has stopped, heal the wound with ointment and other treatments until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of drying from the fire or foundation   (This seems to be incomplete as it's not clear what "of" refers to)
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying from the fire in the intestines and by the constraint of nature, and when the sickness is old and medicine does not work.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	It is necessary that you score the surface of a splinter or your fingernail with a pointed instrument, so it does not get moist.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	then heal it until it heals as it should be.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	and if it cannot heal, then repeat the shaving more forcefully than before, until it heals well, and be cauterized.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then let it heal completely.
dou fremit	great trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont;	Fleas are a small parasite that enters the body deeply;
et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	And sometimes the fever strikes, and it is felt like death due to trembling, spreading throughout the body, more in the hands than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the remedy is that you take a cane of an ostrich feather or a strong eagle's feather and place it on the trembling (part), so that the purple circles surround the trembling completely;
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	then turn your hand all around the cane until you cover the trembling completely and immerse it (the cane) entirely, and dry the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this with a cane of iron or copper according to the following form, and it should be fine-tuned both inside and outside:  (no direct translation for "subtilz desoz et traians desus" which could mean finely made on the inside and smooth on the outside)
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce, to keep it warm and press; and if you see it tremble, cauterize the quiver, as in the chapter of cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the shape of the cluster
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes they make a silver or arsenic suppository, or melted lead or wax; and sometimes they make small and large instruments, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those who are treated in children's care or who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cloister is both small and large, or the bellies are bound in this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez .ij. pertus, et en l’autre .i.;	and it should have an opening where the bellies are bound, as you see, and the chins should be pierced inside; and on one side there are two holes, and in the other one.
et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus,	and the bellies where medicine is put from a beast's bladder or parchment, and should be pierced all around with small holes.
et ait entre chescun pertus .i. doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus .i. fil fort de fil crut tort en .x. ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre;	And place a space between each wound, then push a strong thread through each wound, twisted in ten or more turns around, and bind the belly as if it were a goatskin;
et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And when the medicine is inside [the wound], tie it with a strong thread to the instrument in front, then smear with an ointment; and this is the shape of a circle;
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement;	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with oil or egg yolk ointment, or similar, then push it gently in.
puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses .ij. mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit,	Then the ministers stretch the patient's two hands together until they are completely visible, then remove the cloth and wash the patient's legs.
et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And if the medicine appears to come out, squeeze it as much as possible; and if it does not open for a whole night, it is more beneficial.
