Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is located in the legs, in warm areas where there are no herbs or trees, and in dry land without moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	And sometimes it happens elsewhere than in the legs, which occurs due to rot that comes beneath the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	As it comes within the body and turns, insert a probe between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	If the signs of the beginning of this vein are that it comes in the leg with a very large swelling,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	Then the swelling changes, and the vein begins to emerge, just as a root of a plant does.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the shoulder is opened up, it is necessary that you wrap around it with a piece of wood from one and a half to two feet long, and sew it.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	leave the wood in place on the leg and each time it threatens to slip out, wrap it again with the wood and sew.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	if it is too long, cut off a part of it and wrap the remaining part, but do not cover its root until it is completely out.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	because if you cut it, it will retreat into the flesh and cause abscess or gangrene or other disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	For that thing it is necessary that it be treated little by little up to the head, and nothing remains in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and this vein when it is treated from 5 fingers' length, or 10,
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and once an honest man came to me, from whom the vein issued from 10 fingers' length, and when you cut it, it swelled a little or leaked and pierced all the way down to the bottom,
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	So let everything be empty; and empty the matter that is within, and bring medicine to its place that causes no pain for three days, then heal it as in abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And sometimes at this vein, many raindrops, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot or arm,
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And much blood comes out, from where it jumps out; heal it therefore as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "cattle sickness," because it often affects cattle.
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, which travels through the entire body expanding and contracting,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And it feels to him as if all his limbs are dislocated, until he tears the skin or it jumps forth.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And worms of putrefaction of some humors come towards and snakes, lice, and roundworms or belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And there is doubt about its malice, for when it passes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and comes to the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	Sometimes it enters, and destroys the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see him to cure and drain, one can do it only when he goes:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	therefore, you must lie the limb above and below with a strong cord tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then press on top and pull hard, and if his wound is full to the flesh, you do not draw it out,
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you cauterize the fire on top, until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	And the greater harm it causes is that it runs oil, as we have said;
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it approaching or near the oil, hold a sorcerer's wand beneath it, then strike on top and pull;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	And the patient must use body cleansing with soluble medicines to remove bad humors;
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and if there is corruption of meats, let it be thrown away.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Pain coming from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and moves from member to member; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the armpit of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And afterward, the eye rises like a worm to the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than nothing, just as living silver when it is cut from one piece.
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain divides itself from that place and pierces into the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and a little afterward it runs all through the body until it comes to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then he told me it was returning around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvelled greatly how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Nevertheless, I had often seen pain move from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen it as clearly in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	And I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins exposed.
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore that constrained windiness appears;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and it does not appear according to this reason to those who are ill and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	If the limb above and below is pressed tightly, then press down on it until the swelling is forced back to its place.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the area; if you do not see it with your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	If the cure for these swellings is by pills such as fetid pills and pill of serapion, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows.
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the parts of the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity among them is that some have large points, and small ones, and blunt, and bound ones.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those with two points, and of those with tongues, and of those that have splinters;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and an arrow that strikes any limb does so in two ways: either it pierces through the principal part of the limb, or
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	As a brain, heart, liver, spleen, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it falls in any place of these organs, and the signs of death that I will tell you hereafter will appear to you:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	If you wish to extract this arrow, you must be careful, for death may come in many ways afterwards.
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when this bad sign does not appear at all, and the arrow is not fully embedded, pull it out, and heal the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And when the sign of the skull appears where the arrow strikes the bone, and it breaks through the skull cover,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It is when there are swelling and abscesses, scrofula and eruptions, redness and inflammation of the tongue, spasms and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	And by chance, it may happen without force from the nostrils or ears; and by chance, he may lose speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	And jumps out of the wound white matter resembling pus, and jumps also like boiling tar.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	If this sign appears to you, hold back from the treatment, and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it falls or pierces through is that it is near the left breast and feels as if it has been driven into something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the patient becomes silent like the hair, and in a black blood flow, and coldness and cold sweat comes, and faintness.
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	Therefore, the patient clearly senses death approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	The sign of the arrow that does not pierce the flesh is when bubbles of pus jump out of the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient turns pale, and breathes heavily and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	If the arrow falls on the bedcover of the sick person, it is dislodged from the side ribs; and it releases a lot of fluid and pain and heavy breathing; and all the limbs of the shoulder move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow or food sticks in its wound, by chance something from the indigestible meat might jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow or stomach, and something from the intestine passage might jump out, there is no hope in the treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow strikes in the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, shoulders, shoulders blades, spine of the back, wrists, hips, legs, and similar, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not poisonous, as I shall tell you what happened to me, you do the following.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	A certain man had an arrow lodged or splintered in the root of his neck.
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I drew it out from another side beneath the ear fat and found no injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And drew with force an arrow that had lodged in the oil under the paper underneath,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow was set straight, and it could not reach further than the tip towards the flesh.
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And it was large, the size of a Turkish bow, completely sharp at one end and slightly curved towards the ears; the wound was healed, and no evil accident happened to it.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And passed through an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow had Arabic ears:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I was barbered, and made it thin until I passed through it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And draw an arrow out of a man, who was head or stomach, and thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and then after thirty days, his condition did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut above the arrow, contrived it, drew it out, and had no bad consequences.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if a man receives an arrow in his back or chest, and the wound is sutured;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	And the arrow remained within it, and did not change its natural position.
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor found any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see another man who was pierced by an arrow in his flesh, and the wound was sutured;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	for a long time he endured great pain; and many similar things happened to him.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And draw an arrow from a man of the princes, the king who was stuck in snow.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and he was slightly sloping to the right side; and the arrow was completely lodged.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned for treatment after it had been three days. I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I pierced it with a thin needle and felt nothing.
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	He feels pricking and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was the tip of an arrowhead.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I applied a soothing plaster with digestive properties, because the wounds were not swollen.
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	and the wound of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I place the plaster on for many hours, and heal the wound directly, and keep the patient in that state for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	until he feels the arrow within his neck for one day; and he tells me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I put a corrosive medicine on the wound by hand for many hours until it is cured.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	and I tried it, and felt the head of the arrow that was attached to the place;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	Then align in the opening of the wound with this astringent medicine, until the head of the arrow appears visibly.
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and it passed the boundaries beyond four months.
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And then I closed the wound that I had opened with the tweezers, and it did not heal from one side or the other.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Then I did not cease to refine and to try various instruments until I took a pair of tweezers well made for one day,
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	According to the shape that comes at the end of this chapter, keep following it and return the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	The judgment of the mirrors is that the nose cartilage cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	Then I will restore it, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	Here is the quality of the extraction of some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	If you apply your treatment to this (condition), I do not say all of it, for the books cannot entirely grasp it;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but wise masters understand a little thing, and on this that is failing;
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	true nine work, and it is new invention, in the explanation of things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not enter the limbs where they are inserted except in two ways:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	either through the hole where they enter, or from another side.
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps out from the place where it enters is an arrow entering in a soft part of the body, and sometimes it jumps out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it does not jump out now, leave it until the flesh has healed around it and let the opening be closed.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And similarly, if it [the dislocation] is lodged in the bone and cannot come out, leave it for several days, and move it every day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	Then it jumps, and if it does not jump, pierce around it with a sharp awl wherever the joint is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	If the arrow is lodged in the skull bone and reaches one of the brain cavities,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	And some of the accidents that I have mentioned to the patient: do not draw it out at all, but let it remain equal after several days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	if an arrow comes up to such a point, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	If the arrow has not pierced beyond the bone but only comes up to this point,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And the patient remains for several days without any bad accidents, then attempt to draw it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot be withdrawn, administer tourniquets around it, as I have told you; then heal the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if an arrow is lodged inside the body so it cannot be seen, press all around it.
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	And if you feel it, pull it out with any suitable tool.
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	And if it cannot be done due to the narrowness of the wound and the deepness of the arrowhead,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and there is no bone, nerve, or vein, so make an incision as wide as the wound is large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	draw out the arrow if possible, and if there are ears on the arrow like hooks to hold onto it,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	If bone the flesh which is pierced by two parts in the muscles that you can feel,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the arrowhead until you can pull it out.
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	be careful not to break the arrow, so that you can pull it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it at once, press the flesh around it, then pull it out, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the flow of blood opposes (the procedure), bring what we have said about its treatment in its chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and guard yourself from cutting the nerve and the vein, and use an instrument as you can pull out the arrow without risk.
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; place the patient according to the shape he was in when the arrow hit him.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	because it is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot, place him according to what the signs indicate to you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	Arrow that comes from elsewhere, if you open anything related to it, or the skin is swollen in some place as can be seen or felt:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Then cut, so long as the pliers can grasp it, and then pull it out; if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, then round your hand and push it into the bone, expand the bone, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, leave it for now, and then continue the extraction until it comes out.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	And if it were of an arrow inside, push it all out.
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	and if it were a dislocation, and you wish to administer treatment, give one instrument of traction.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; then push forcefully.
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	and if the arrow is covered, place one sharp instrument at its point to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow has been touched, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if possible.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	then heal the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow falls or penetrates the belly, bladder, side, or chest and is near, and you can cover it, then do so.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	but be careful not to cut the vein and the nerve, then pull it out, and then stitch the wound if necessary.
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And the treatment while it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shapes of the tweezers used to extract arrows are similar to an eagle's beak, and here is their shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The form of the hair root is like the feather of a bird.
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	To point the arrowhead, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of pliers for pointed and for measuring, as shown here:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of veins in the human body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	From veins from which one recovers are 31, of which the head is 16,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	this means: it is known, two veins that are after the ears, which are called the "double 'herbech'" [literally, double herbs];
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	and the two arteries that are in two temples visible;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	and the two veins that are in the hollows of the two eyes, which are called "aspirers" [literally, inspirers];
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	1) and the vein which is on the forehead;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	3) and the two arteries which are in the neck;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	4) and the two veins that are in the upper lip above the mouth, and these veins are called "augeherich";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	5) and the two veins which are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins commonly used for letting blood are 5 in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side of the chest, and the common people call it "vein of the head";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	and the median (the one that was called "faste" in earlier times) is composed of the cephalic and the basilic.
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And the lay people call it "vein of the heart"; and the abscess is located on the right side.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And the lay people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the liver.
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	This is the one that heals, which opens clearly above the navel.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	The saviatelle is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two rains (joints).
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	And in the leg and foot there are 3 veins: one is beneath the hollow of the left thigh,
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	The second saphenous vein which is at the right ankle; and the vein called "anse," which is in the left ankle;
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg there are 3 veins beneath those (veins).
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The vein that is after the ears helps with ancient catarrhs and migraines.
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of the healer, as I tell you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	and rub the place where the veins or veins are with a rough cloth; then hold the patient's neck with a screw.
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head.
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then cut them with a knife where you feel the pulse beneath your hand,
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	Then take the lance, and thrust it beneath the vein until the bone, then pull your hand along the entire vein.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And pierce the skin and the vein well with two fingers deep through, and make the blood come out as much as you see.
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then tie it and let it be until it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	And I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The sanitation of the two arteries which are in the two temples, is worth ancient migration, [in modern English: The cleaning of the two arteries located in the two temples has an old-fashioned curative effect]
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	and softening, and eye treatment that is common, and for the eyes with inflamed glands;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	and the qualities of sanitation are as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	and it is that the patient extends his neck, until both veins appear clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	And feel the pulses beneath your throat, then press on them.
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift the vein at the top of your neck, near the artery, and push the needle under it.
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	lift the vein upwards and tie it off, as you have done in the two other veins, and stop the blood flow according to your need.
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, and place your hand on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then form the ligature (a type of stitch or binding), and leave it until it heals; we have spoken about its covering and its removal, where the book begins.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The healing of the vein in the forehead is as effective as the healing of the cranial wounds from the ancient facial diseases that have migrated and turned red.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	The quality is such that the patient stretches their neck while twisting it, until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the instrument called "fossoir", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the point on the vein, and press up from your hand, or something else, and let the blood flow according to the quantity that you see;
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein when it is healthy and not at any time should the operation be done with a large flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Moreover, the flame should not be too sharp; and the vein should be cut across because the bone is nearby, and by chance, the flame may break if it is too thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The cutting of the two veins that are in each eyelid helps with the eyes, and with the temple, and with the jaw, and with the ear in oil, and with diseases of the face;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the qualities of their sanity are such that the patient stretches their neck in twisting with any cord, as before.
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then the sanity, and it is the sanitizer of the cross, a small length of fire, a little wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flame is fine, perhaps it breaks; then make the sanitizer of the blood, as much as you need, and then lay it on cloth, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The sanitizer of the vein from the neck is useful against ague, scrofula, and diseases of the face.
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	If it swells and reddens as if coming out in a boil, especially when it is old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	and the characteristics of the pus are such that the patient compresses his neck, then squeezes his nose with your left hand.
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	and take the subtle flame long, and thrust it into the gap between the two nostrils.
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	for the veins do not open well there, and the blood will soon begin to flow.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And do not go too deep, and correct the blood according to your necessity, then tie it for a night, for it is soon restored.
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The salves of the two kinds aid in the treatment of ulcers, the beginning of leprosy, and many diseases, and in stopping pustules, corrosion, eruptions, and sores.
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the qualities of the salve are that the patients stretch their necks under both arms, as we have said.
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the master stand over the head of the sick person, and the sick person sit on one seat,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then open the vein along a long stretch, then draw out the blood moderately, as needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then repair another vein on the other side, then untie the ligature, and gently compress all the veins,
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The patient should not strangle [himself]; and he should leave it until morning so that the wound is healed.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the healing of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The healing of the wounds on the lips above helps with the congestion in the mouth and corruption of gums, and cuts or cracks in the lips, as well as toothaches and around.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the qualities of the wound are to have the patient sit before you, and hold his neck as I said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right side of the lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	and they can be recognized because they are black, and because there are small veins surrounding them:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Therefore take both, and if you do not know them, and you have doubts,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If you strike the largest of each part, and similarly make incisions in the two veins that are above and below, for it is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	Draining the saliva under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	Draining the veins that are under the tongue helps after the cranial drainage and is used for narrowing of the throat, eye diseases, and mouth diseases.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	And the quality of draining is that the patient lies on their back before the sun, lifts the tongue, and looks down at each side to find a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Keep then one and the other, and do not go too deep, for below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The incisions in the body, which are commonly healed in two ways:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	or with a sharp point, large mirret flame or subtle olive oil like you measure, and it is called "anesil".
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they (veins) are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of fire mirrhine is very famous, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It is necessary to open veins that are swollen and filled with thick, troubled blood.
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And this is the form of olive oil fire:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more subtly pointed out, and is for healing subtle veins where there is subtle, citrus-colored blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The basilica vein (one of the subtle veins), helps with diseases that are below the throat, neck, chest, and abdomen.
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And the master should drain it skillfully and make sure to avoid the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if it pierces the artery, and bleeding comes out, it should be cauterized, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	but must not be pricked by the flame, but cut like a needle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the bladder does not open manifestly, you should open it and change another one.
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	or you wish to have any drain from it, or you heal in its place the vein into the arm: it opens manifestly;
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the cup to the fire anoint, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you wish to know the location of the wound, then it is necessary that you straighten the arm and touch the place where you feel the pulse.
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	Then sign the wound, then bind the arm, and burn the vein with fire.
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And be careful not to cut into the artery when you see it swollen, for that is the artery; therefore, avoid cutting into it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it rise high like the urine of a child, and the wound is red and delicate, know that it is not from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Then place your hand on top for a long time, then cut through the wound where it is red, because often there are:
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	tie the arm and leave it like that, do not move it for the patient; and be careful, do not move it until it becomes clean.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the wound is not bleeding and it swells, and the medicine is not present, then cut open the artery if it is open, because it will shrink; and stop the bleeding from the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a piece of fennel root, cut it and take one half and bind it firmly until the next day;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If it does not stop bleeding, that is good; if not, heal it as we have said, with powders that stop blood.
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	and the application of cauterization should not be applied in various conditions due to the small size of the wound and the thickness of the ligament in the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The vein in the middle helps to drain blood from the head above, and from the body below.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	and it is necessary for the surgeon to wander along the nerve that is below, and if it pricks too deeply, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	and it inflames and the patient may get sick, and perhaps cannot recover;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens wide many times, and if it does not open in any man due to its subtlety, then you must draw the instrument anesthetic on it; and pull the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	If there is a vein between the two nerves, make it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The sanity of the cephalic helps, that it draws blood from the head, and helps the eyes;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to cauterize by pricking with the olive oil flame or the myrtle flame, for it is the safest of all veins, for there is no nerve or artery below it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Furthermore, you must seek the most accessible joint, and do not cause harm in the first attempt, and you can start again.
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And occasionally veins swell up in some men, in which case, do not cause harm in the first attempt.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the wound, according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about treating wounds is that wound treatment is not brought about except to preserve health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to prevent diseases from coming.
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And the wound should be treated in one of the four veins that are cut: namely, cephalic, facial, and basilic.
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And it should be bled at the beginning of springtime in goose, and in autumn and winter after eating, when signs of saturation appear;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And it should be bled the first day or third day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The bleeding that is administered for diseases has no fixed hour, but whenever need be, either day or night, at all hours and in every instance.
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it should not be bled children under 12 years old, nor women carrying a child until the fourth month after conception up to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	One should not heal the elderly who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when someone wants to be healed in any way, it is necessary that their intestines be cleansed with a gentle enema.
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if they have retained many feces, so that the veins are not able to expel the superfluidities which could harm the main limbs.
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	one should not heal those who are excessively salted with foods, drunk, until they recover, or those who have dropsy.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	and if he is wounded after colic affliction, vomiting, abdominal distension, excessive copulation with women, hard work, staying up late, and all that weakens the strength, or by something related to the weapon or the body;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	then purify the bodily fluids, if they are large, through food and drinks and medications, if you have that ability;
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	afterwards take a bath, unless something prevents it, to purify the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	And heal the vein with the wound around the third part, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	Keep him that day from work, and from pain, and from lust, and similar things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And be lying down and comfortable, and let the healer be higher than the one being healed, and rub the arm two or three times;
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then draw out the ligature slightly, because if it is too tight or loose, it cannot heal properly;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the joint with hands until the veins swell, and feel them.
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the bladder with a little bit of old oil and place your thumb of your left hand on top of that vein beneath the joint as much as you want to cauterize it.
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not burst or split when striking (or cutting).
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that behave like strings in the bladder, and some are filled with windiness.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	If you put it over the flame, if you remove from the flame, and it cannot open the vein, and thus it is one of these.
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if it opens the vein, but the wound is too narrow, then the surgeons should be aware of such things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, that is good; if not, then continue a little more under that level or quickly above it, if the area is not inflamed.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the area is inflamed and the patient becomes frightened, leave him for one or two days and do not bind his arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance, an abscess may come; do not enter a bath, then resume the healing if it pleases him.
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the perforation is small or the wound subtle, and you doubt whether it will not bleed as much as you see, then be bold in that same perforation with full flame directly.
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and open it a little hastily, so that the flesh is inflamed; for this happens often when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the flesh inflamed, do not resume the healing, and put a little oil on it, for the oil cools the blood and is congealed in that place by the oil.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And thus administer the remedy of oil in each wound that you open veins, to stop the flow of blood.
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And this same thing should be ground and boiled from them when it is placed on the wound; if it becomes too thick, grind it again to make it finer.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	If an abscess becomes large, which often happens when the wound is not opened until that time,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you are in a hurry, place a damp and warm sponge on the wound and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary that you do this after the evacuation of blood from the vein, and if it remains in place after several days without any blackness or greenness, it does not harm him.
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see, place something of aloes or myrrh below the wound, poultice, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and appearance in the sanctuary of the basilica; therefore, put your hand on it, and if you feel it soft under the pressure of your hand, then it is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not place anything on it from what we have said, because by chance, in court without the artery; but make one dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with other treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And draw blood from each according to the quantity of its power, and of the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it become thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for one who is full and hollow, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and let the veins be wide.
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and it is necessary to bleed little and often, and it should be bled by cutting across, not by pricking.
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	and this method of bloodletting is safe from disorder of the blood and damage to the nerve, and it is more effective than long bleeding or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for one whose body needs bloodletting, it is necessary to give moistened bread below pomegranate seeds; if he is chilled, draw blood four or six times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And if it is of cold constitution, feed it with soft bread soaked in sweet syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil,	And if it swells after the evacuation of blood, then it is necessary for him to drink broth made from charcoal and fragrant subtle syrup.
et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	and use other things as we have said in the section or chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to dislocate his arm, and strain it another time, if necessary, when it is weakened by excessive strain, it should heal little by little, according to the quantity of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to dislocate his arm after the first strain, and it has rest for nine hours after the first strain, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to heal from another part, should heal within two days or three.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson;	Because there is much blood inside the body that has already become heated and causes fever; therefore, it is necessary to draw a large amount and to widen the opening until it yields pus.
puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	then you heal all the conditions of health, and place your hand on top of the toes when it is healthy, so that death does not come in place of pus.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	and this happens often, when healers are negligent;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	and it is not necessary that you dislocate the arm, make blood flow a second time, and the wound has closed, but you should push firmly;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it is curved, extend the arm as much as possible, for it would not be good.
mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer,	Leave it until it heals the second time; or you pierce it with the tip of the flame, until the coagulated blood from the vein has flowed out.
et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and put on one piece of new linen soaked in hot water and press slightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and do not squeeze it until the abscess is soothed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, do so in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is drawn from the vein of the head because it is composed [of the same thing].
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of drawing blood is that the patient places their hand in hot water until the vein turns red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then tie it moderately, so that the vein appears clearly, then press it firmly with your fingers, not too wide nor too long.
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	and make the cuts wide, and press firmly near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be pierced, press the hot water into it, let the blood flow out into the hot water until you have enough.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it is summer, do not press the hot water into it, because it puts more in winter than in summer.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the vein of this one [vein] is safer than all other veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The vein of the left arm saves [all] liver diseases, and this is how it works:
estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie;	hold the hand, and push in hot sharp [object], until the vein has escaped, if you can see it.
et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien;	And if the vein is crossed, and you cut it all through, it causes no harm.
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char,	And do not go too deep, because the nerves are entirely bare under the skin,
et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Then replace the hand in hot water, so that it does not freeze in the wound, and is unable to come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have bled the blood as much as necessary, put oil and linen on the wound to heal quickly, and do the same for each wound.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The sore on his left hand is beneficial for the sickness of mice, and do as I told you regarding the right one.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The sore in the chest is beneficial for all diseases that are beneath the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	like the illnesses of the belly, and retention of fluids, and the sickness of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And the quality of his health is such that the patient should put his foot in hot water and rub it over the vein until it bleeds.
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	and on top of the ankle-joint, and the vein is located below the foot, and it should be rubbed much with oil.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	then let him use the larger vein or one at the ankle, which is more useful.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if [you] pierce it through the skin that is below, pierce also in the same way as in cutting; and let the flame be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if [the skin] cannot be pierced out, place the point in the water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it requires suturing for the first time, begin a second time a little higher because the skin is salty.
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And do not be afraid of the nerve, as we have said, and likewise proceed with the suturing of the other foot equally.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The head of the sciatic nerve is located at the knee joint, and its pain resembles that of the heel when it is hot with blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville .iiij. dois en tordant,	And the qualities of its pain are such that the patient immerses himself or herself in hot water up to the knee joint, while twisting the leg four times.
car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, you should treat it in all possible ways and by crossing it.
et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	and it is necessary that you cut it, for the nerve is withdrawn, and it is very difficult to touch with hands.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners;	And if you don't pull it [the bone or limb] out correctly, no remedy will open or heal its back or its end, and beware of the nerves;
et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	Make the vein bleed as much as possible so that you see it, then tie it and place cotton on it and press; it is now healed.
Des sainies de ventouse	Venous Sutures (or stitching)
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Venous ligatures (or stitching) are made of horns, antler, or glass; and venous ligation is done in two ways: by making an incision and drawing blood, or without making an incision.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this ventosation, which is caused to wound, exists in two ways: it is either for all fires or with fire;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	and this ventosation which is made by wounding and extraction of blood is performed in fourteen places of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	because one is located in the head entirely; and the others are in the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	and two others in the sides of the neck; and the ventosations under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the boils on the two shoulders; and the boils on the calves.
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	The above line translates to: "And the boils on the two arms; and the boils on the two legs."
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	And the boils on the two ankles; and the ventosation does not treat blood, except for minor veins that are scattered in the flesh.
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	And therefore it should not be done at all, like we do with venesection of veins.
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And it should not be administered, neither with all fire nor fire sense, in any disease that comes from swelling, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	If there is a need for bloodletting due to illness, or by custom, we shall administer it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and at midday and every time.
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need bloodletting, have a heavy head;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	And for those who find swelling and redness in their body, head, or neck, the eyes should be held steady.
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	And for those who find a spot of blood in their mouth and have swollen the tongue, and are bleeding;
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And for those who think they are pregnant, and see dark blood and abort and die, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we observe these signs, especially if it is within the month, we order to fumigate after 4 hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The purging of the mouth helps alleviate the headache that comes to the eyes; and it should not be done after the evacuation of all the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	...and this ventilation is in place of the purging of the head.
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	and it should not be used by those with a cold complexion or who have constipation, as it causes them great harm.
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	...and therefore it should not be used by the elderly or those with cold head diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And he who recovers often becomes negligent, and for this reason it is necessary to place the cupping glass slightly lower due to the doubt of negligence.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	The cupping at the neck is in the place of the recovery of the head and the basilica, and for this reason it is beneficial for the fracture of the bone.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	and to cut through the channel of the throat, and immediately, and to fill (it).
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it must be pushed gently, for if it holds too firmly, it may cause obstruction in the intestine or stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as .ij. costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens,	The ventosation of the two ribs from the neck is worth the pains in the head, and otalgia and migraines, and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth.
et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And it is in the position of the basilica artery; and you must command the Lord to extend his hand, so that he does not cut the artery, and there should be no flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventosations (ventosation) beneath the chin is useful for mouth diseases and gum corruption, and similar oral ailments; and it is located in the vicinity of the salivary glands of the two lower lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The ventosations (ventosation) of the shoulder is useful for diseases caused by heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des .iij. voinnes dou bras,	The ventosations (ventosation) of the ribs are as effective as four veins in the arm,
car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes;	For it attracts blood from these large veins;
et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	and instruct the lord not to pierce too deeply, for the limb is bare of flesh, and knows beneath dark and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The poultice that is on the buttocks is useful for piles from their foundation and diseases below, and it should be large, made of flax, which needs to be well drawn out; and by chance, if it were fine, it would break; and it causes big wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Poultices on the legs heal quickly because they draw blood from the entire body, and are useful for old pains in the knees and ankles, and bladder and urinary tract problems, and remove inflammation; and they are located between the two shins and two ankles, and weaken the body over a long period of time, causing swelling in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting on the bladder is that you first empty it, and fill it promptly, and place it hastily, and move it equally, and not cease doing so until you see the area turn red and swell, and appear the color of blood; then tie, and replace the bladders, and take care in the positioning of the body, for there are some who have soft flesh and clear veins: it is necessary to pierce only once, and it is necessary to make large incisions, and one shallow; and suck lightly.
