Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	If the flesh is thick, it is necessary to pierce twice: the first time to refine the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	If the flesh is very thick, it is necessary to pierce the third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we should only prick once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish to have much blood, let us frequently remedy it; and if the wound is closed, break it open thoroughly, and let the veins be pierced quickly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And for those with thick and hard skin, and with narrow pores, you should anoint the joints of the armpits with stimulating and dissolving oil.
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	if it is in summer, use violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or seed oil of cucumber.
et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if it is ivy, oil of watercress, lilies, chamomile, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is thick and cold, take amaranth oil, or balsam oil, or anise oil, and similar.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile,	And if the one whose wound is to be healed has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be applied.
mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	But it should be washed after the ventilation with rose water, cold water, water of blackberries, water of cucumber, water of porcelain, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And he who has much moisture should rise from ashes of myrtle, or water of bilberry, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans;	And those with excessive fluids should rise from old wine or juice of sourdock, or decoction of fennel or chamomile, or similar things.
et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou .ij.; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion,	and it is not necessary to let the blood before bath or in bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and do not sleep after bloodletting.
et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it is necessary that he urinates when he should let blood and after bloodletting.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez;	And watch for the patient who is sanguine and bilious, and if he is too sharp and inflamed;
si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses;	then it is necessary that he take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces in the form of juice;
et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	and cook peas, meat of chicken, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons;	And he who has a cold complexion, should take syrup of honey and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and eat barley meal, and drink barley porridge and small birds and young birds.
et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier;	and the day when he will vomit, he must drink more than eat;
et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz;	It is necessary to give some men sometimes tricolor or muscat before or after vomiting, to strengthen the main members.
et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And the wine must be made subtle, but it must not be drunk by those who are hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The blisters placed on wounds are those placed on the liver, spleen, gout, abdomen, kidney, and loins, because these members cannot bear to be wounded there.
et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre,	and it is done only to draw blood from one member to another,
si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus lou ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre;	as we do with the testicles when they are swollen; to remove the thickening in the member, just as we place blisters on the abdomen and the loins to reduce its size.
et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And alleviate the pain when there is an obstruction or arrow, if possible it draws the obstruction by its attracting virtue, or removes the arrow from its place.
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And so it is done when placed upon the liver and spleen where there is retained wind.
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these windy conditions are treated with emptiness to suck only; sometimes they are treated with fire, and sometimes filled with cold water.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	as in diseases of the lungs, and in this manner the windy condition is filled with hot water, or cold water where there has been cooked comfrey herbs.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the bladder (or cupping glass) treated with fire is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	It should have two fingers' width in length and half a palm in depth, and it should have one small hole on each side, similar to the size of pushing an awl.
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	and it should be made of horn or leather in front so that it does not burn the patient when placed on the limb.
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And have in the middle a rod of iron or steel, to make an incision, a puncture.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and be large or small according to the diseases and age of those who suffer them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	because the swellings of children are different from those of adults, and thin people from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And this swelling should be placed on the limb in this way:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Use a candle of wax or linen thread, and place it through the hole in the syringe that is in the plunger.
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the light is at the bottom of the syringe so as not to burn the patient;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and your hands should be above the wound as we have said, so that when you see it, if steam goes out, remove the syringe.
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And wrap it with linen as before, and repeat often if needed.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In the bladder that is administered in a case of pleurisy, there should be neither prick nor puncture, and it should not be used unless when it is full of fluid, and placed on the member only.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Incisions are not applied except to members where it is not possible to apply leeches due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar places;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and in bare skin areas, such as the hand or neck, and other similar places;
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	and it is known that when you find leeches in clean, sweet and clear water, you may take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and put them in clean water until they are accustomed to it and have nothing in their stomachs;
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	And then let it be bled from the vein and from the blisters, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place sulphur on it.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	And when they are full and hot, if it is a place where a blister can be applied, do so, because it is very effective.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If there is no place for a blister, lift the wound from ashes, then with water, very well, and then sprinkle it.
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	And if the wounds heal too quickly due to the sulphur, moisten one linen cloth with cold water and place it on top until the wound is healed.
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	And if the wound is multiplying, apply powdered vitriol (or something similar), and let it dry until it is completely dried.
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	Apply half a handful of peeled beans to the wound and let it stay until it dries and stops bleeding.
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	and if you need more, take other snakesbane (a potent poison).
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the snakesbane is not available, apply fresh blood to the wound and insert an awl until the poison comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	And then place [them] on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they bleed.
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are bleeding, sprinkle some aloe and crushed linseed or ashes over it, then they will stop bleeding now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine and concerns the treatment of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Inform the foolish child that the madman throws himself out of this chapter, that he never saw any old books or read any letter from them.
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	and because of this reason, knowledge is estranged in our land, for I never found anyone good with it.
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	and I know nothing else except by the knowledge of old books, where I have studied the science, and through experience, and the custom of my life.
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described to you in this chapter what it contains, and I have summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the shapes of the instruments that are brought in, as I have done in these 2 chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, let us now say the prologue of this book, the subjects in which wisdom places its understanding, and dwell on truth, so that those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when breakage or dislocation or twisting or swelling comes to anyone, you should hasten to heal the patient from both sides, unless something prevents it, such as weakness of the body, infancy, or old age;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the time is not very hot or too cold, and if it consumes cold foods, specifically cold meats such as eye of round and veal, and does not drink wine nor consume any fatty meats, and does not fill itself too much with meats that fill the veins with blood, until you have doubt about the abscess heating up or spreading matter in the limb; then the patient returns to his first treatment as he has used it.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that make good nourishment or have thickness, such as cooked wheat in water, meat, head, feet, pork, eggs, fresh fish, strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this nourishment, the bones heal faster and sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	And know that the broken bones of the elderly and weak cannot be well recovered or mended according to their nature due to the fragility of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children.
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But there is no cure, reset the broken bone, i.e. large tendons that bind and join the limb together until it heals as it was before; and not let him do any work, and for this reason, nourish him with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the fractures are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the hip, or the leg; and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that heals by itself, and another that becomes sharper, like the tip of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a fracture with an open wound, or one with just a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each kind there is its tool and proper instrument for restoration, as memory comes to mind.
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	And it is known that the bone break occurs when the place is twisted, widely open by dislocation, and sounds when compressed by the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And if there is no twisting or pressure, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no break.
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	But it may have a twist, fracture, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	Do not move the hand, but put on medications that come after this, and then hold it gently now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the breaks that go to the artery, and are the two parts disjoined, they should now be set equally, thus the abscess will heal well.
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if an abscess comes, let it be left for some time until the abscess is calm.
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then equalize it to the bone that you can easily and skillfully move, and know that the restoration of it is easier than the restoration where there are pieces; then bind it as described hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	If the bone is broken into pieces, if it is in the foot or hand, or with one hand if it is a small member, or with two ropes, or with one rope and one hand:
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	And put the limb according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the member are disjoined, you reset them by every means possible in their original positions, and make sure through your work that the patient does not suffer injury or pain.
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	Align well the two bones of the joint according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	Feel it with your hand if it seems not to be well aligned: straighten it nicely and do not strain or press too much as those who apply pressure through their work cause abscesses and contractions in the limb, as we have often observed.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is broken, cautiously immobilize the patient so that they do not move, whether awake or sleeping, turning, or in any other way.
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And ensure that the limb is securely set so that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For if it feels no pain, then it has not been properly set and must be re-set in such a way that it feels no pain.
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	Ensure that it is put rightly, for twisting will result when it is restored.
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And the qualities of a broken limb are as I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs come in various shapes, sizes and forms.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, like fingers, toes, and such: you must wrap linen cloths that are soft and thin around them.
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And those who are fat, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to wrap with a wide and hard bandage, for the large bandages embrace the entire large member and equally constrict from all sides, so that there is no sore.
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie light bandages around it, 3 or 4 times according to the member, and hold your hand a little on the entire bandage, then go above the break and constrict less, so that the break is constrained. Then move away a little from the break.
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And soften the bandage little by little, until you take a large part of the healthy side, then take another bandage and wrap it directly over the broken place.
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then go to the part under the break, and hold it gently, not too strongly nor too loosely, as we have said in the first place above.
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then put cotton threads or cloth strips equal in length between the joints, then tie it all up with bandage, and then put well-made splints on top if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there is an abscess or swelling, place something soothing and warm on top of it to help with the abscess and reduce swelling, and leave it like that for some days.
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then hold your arm-lengths (approximately half a cane) firmly, either with a saw or a plaster rod, or with palm branches, and they should be shaped as follows:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	But the arm-lengths that one places on the break should be a little thicker and wider than the others.
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and should also be as long as necessary for the small or large limb.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	Then hold above the shoulders in the same way you did at the first location, then tie upwards with a thread as on the first location on the fracture.
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	Then pull tighter but not too much, and it is necessary that the thread be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of fine linen.
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	for if the thread is thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who make their knots with twisted linen cords, and this is a great error, because the knot cannot be even if it is too thin, and it is not good that there should be less than two fingers' space between each shoulder.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient has a splinter in his shoulder bones after setting them in healthy places, place lin or wool padding over it to prevent bleeding.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a break and the veins are cut open, I will tell you the cure below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	Know that it is not necessary to set all broken limbs immediately on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not necessary to set bones forcefully before 5 or 7 days, or more according to your certainty of the abscess healing.
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of ancient plasters for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: you shall take flour that is kept in the mill walls, and mix it with an abundance of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it; this is the common method for restoring a fracture in various ways, and especially for women and small children, for it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Here is another method of plaster for restoring fractures and dislocations and twists: take barley meal, linseed oil, elder, marshmallow root, mastic, anise, cinnamon, and gum arabic, mix them in equal parts; add myrrh, aloeswood, and seven times as much alkanet root; make this into a powder and mix it with enough egg; if the complexion of the patient is hot, use this plaster, for it has a good composition and restores broken bones quickly, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster for twisting: take mastic and marshmallow root, mix them in equal parts; add myrrh and aloeswood, seven times as much; beat well, then combine with vinegar or enough egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of plaster for joints and dislocated bones, soothe the pain occurring, and cut the bone, and break it: take new linen, wet it in vinegar and cooked oil, and place it on the affected area. This plaster does not restore, but it is good for easing abscess heat, and treating bone pain properly.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that sets broken bones: take dried leaves of the fig tree and leaves of ground ivy, grind them together, and make plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of bone fractures and to hasten the healing of abscesses. Take roots of mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, a part of each; grind them together, add wine, and if the limbs are scalded, use moist coriander water instead, or plain water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another method of plastering, more forceful than the first, when the restoration of a limb comes due after an abscess has hardened. Take roots of mugwort, flax, balm, sweet clover, and sage, as well as flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; grind them up, and cook with salt water, sweet water, or wine, according to the heat of the member, and its state of rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates says in his book that nothing other than beeswax and oil should be put on a broken limb to restore it, and it should not be too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It appears Galen says that dry and slightly warm substances should be put on a broken limb to restore it, such as myrrh, aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of plaster that is beneficial for injuries and pain: take ground mugwort and crushed human hair, or feathers of birds, and equal parts of vismale and oil, and grind them together, and make a plaster from the mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	Then wait a little while after that, and make sure the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; do not dislocate it for many days.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	If pain or itching occurs at the site, or there is no rest, swelling, or inflammation, hurry and dislocate it immediately, remove the plaster now; take a light cloth, sea sponge moistened with seawater, and immerse the affected area until the itching stops and the pain is relieved.
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the member rest for an hour, then place dry linen on it, dampen in vinegar or rose oil, and tie it above with a nut, until you are sure of heating the abscess.
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	and let the inflammation of the member rest, and the pain be removed, then begin the binding again subtly, and a little plaster, and do not strain it too much as before; bind subtly until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has subsided and the redness, pain, and swelling have been removed from all parts, and you need plaster and linen, then begin again as you did before equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if no swelling comes to the limb as we have said, do not release it before 3 or 4 or 5 or 7 days; and sometimes leave it for 20 days, according to what one sees, until the break heals, and the dislocation approaches the flesh.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Then hold it more tightly and the flesh swells, as I said before; and if you see the limb drying out more than necessary, know that nourishment cannot enter.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Then apply hot moist heat to the area every time you release it, and this should be done three times a day, and slightly loosen the bandage.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	By this work therefore cut the nerves in the limb and fix carefully what the foolish doctors do, who twist the limb: it is harmful, and it is a fearful work, and I see nothing but to weaken and to work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	There are many ways of breaks, and various shapes, and the causes are intended.
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	For it has breaks made by sword blows, and the hilt strikes the whole bone up to the shaft that is beneath the bone, as happens in a hack or thrust; and for this reason, this method of breaking is called "hack-wound".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the sword strikes the bone from above, it is called this type of break "absolute"; and the wound caused by these two breaks can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded percussion, or a fracture or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a persistent break that approaches the membrane located beneath the bone or above it, and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if the wound heals against the bone as thinly as hair, and the fracture is small, and because of this it is called a "hairline" fracture.
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	and if the wound is made by striking with stone or falling, or something similar, and forces the bone piece inside, and the fracture is closed like a potter when he puts it on the pottery oven; if the stone is inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	And this happens more often in those who have or a moist bone head, like a child's head;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	and it occurs in all these ways of fracture where small pieces are dislodged, like this; and I will speak about its treatment.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	We should know all the ways of fractures by traction above them, and the probe for tenting, and the corruption of flesh that is above it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair-like appearance is known by this: when one exposes the bone and rubs above it, if the fracture opens black,
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, be aware of the symptoms of the patient; and if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of senses, extension, swelling, fever, and hairs to fall out and turn red, and other similar signs in various dispositions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an uncertain accident, and you hope for salvation, begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when a wound first comes to you in winter, you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day if possible.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is a fracture, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue beneath the bone is not corrupted, and the consequences as we have said come about.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the fracture of the bone reaches the tissue that covers the brain, you must cut along the broken part in this way: and it is that you take hold of the patient's head with your left hand, and expose the bone above in all possible ways, and on the surface of the wound more gently than you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	and if there is discharge of blood in uncovering the bone or an abscess formed, help it as necessary, and it is that you fill the area with dampened linen soaked in rose oil.
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And make the wound rest until the abscess has calmed down and you are assured of the flow of blood; then begin around the bone to remove, and this is done according to two ways of working: one way is that you cut at a narrow incision in front, and this is called the first method.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	Then make another incision larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have many incisions of various sizes, some narrow and others wide, sharp and made of iron; and work gently so as not to pierce the bone.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is pushed out and hard, you must pierce it around, so that you provide holes with drills, but not so deep that they pass through the bone to the skin; and it should have a margin or circle on top where the point does not pass beyond the bone; and you must have several, so that each one comes in its place at the thickness of the bone, so that you have drills for all places; and this is the form of the four kinds of drills:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place one drill on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then remove the drill a little to one side, and do this all around, and then cut the space of the bone between the fractures, making it as thinly and gently as possible, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand or any of the tools you have, such as pliers or tweezers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the marrow.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and treated the bone, it is necessary that you remove the compacted part that remains of the bone with an instrument resembling a cutter, but it must be thinner and more delicate than the other cutters.
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there remain small bones or no scales, gently remove them with tools; then treat the wound with the remedies we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of work is that which the Greeks call, which is more secure; and they highly praise it, and this is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must cut open a part of the bone where the fracture has moved apart, so that when you have exposed that part, you will place the lenticular anvil underneath it as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And it shall not be cut from one side, and the parts are sharp on two edges, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly break the bone all around, and be careful of the cloth that is beneath.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is adhered to the bone, break it gently, for it is broken badly and with fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone does not break through the cloth, and the bone is only chopped from above, and there are small pieces, then you must follow that roughness, and remove the scales with a sharp razor, which you should have in various quantities, to provide the most convenient amount for each place, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If (the patient) shaves very closely at first, and afterward with something more subtle, and does not cease doing so until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each other type of haircut and break (injury), you must bring about the remedy according to his condition; this is not something that can be answered by one who has devoted study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is open, then you must take one piece of linen, according to the size of the wound, and wet it in rose oil, and put it on the wound.
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	then take another piece of linen doubled either twice or four times, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and put it on the first linen; and do this more gently so as not to hurt the wound, then administer another ligature, but do not tighten it more than necessary to cover the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And let it remain for one day or two, until the abscesses subside, then release it, and administer medicines like those of lilies, flour of wheat, incense powder, aromatics, and similar things; and from these things make powder, and place it on the wound, and administer immediately medicines without harm or poison.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And ensure that the wound is always clean, do not let any salve or pus accumulate, nor let it collect blood, for when pus accumulates on the brain cloth, it will rot and fester, causing great harm to the patient; for when something biting is applied, it causes pain by pressing from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, beware of any bad accidents happening to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful with great certainty.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if blackness does not come forcefully except for medicine that has been placed upon it, whose virtue is such, then you must take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in gum apply one piece of linen cloth, and place it thereon.
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the care should be done according to wound treatments until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one by itself, because there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break, but instead causes swelling or twisting, and then heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must insert your little finger or thumb into the nose, and place the break equal to the index finger inside the nose, and to the mouth by force, until the nose returns according to its natural shape.
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the nose and the finger cannot reach the place, you must place it equal to the knuckle of a finger (a thumb) on top of the nose.
Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, mend it thus, and hasten to restore it within the first day, if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then bind to the head of the wound with linen cloths if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Tie another piece of linen on the other side if the break is there; let the cloths be thick enough to fill the wounds of the head.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	They said that any restoration should be moistened with butter and changed every day. I do not think it is good, but they should be moistened in a mixture of egg white and flour; then leave the cloth until the bone is hard, and the cartilage becomes hard.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers from an owl are placed instead of tweezers, and if there is a single soft cloth around it, and the breakage is held, and the patient breathes through it; then do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If an abscess bursts while you are working on it, place camphor or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a pinch of alum.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis;	If the abscess does not burst, apply plaster outside of it, made from flour of wheat and powder of incense, mixed with egg white, then place light bandages on top but do not tie the abscess.
et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu;	And if the break in the neck is small and it is broken into small pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then make the incision, and the treatment of such things with healing charms, suturing, as plasters and ointments suitable for this purpose.
et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no wound within the neck, treat it with bandages, and place planks of wood on it until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	The treatment for a jaw fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible (jawbone) is dislocated beneath, and there is no wound outside, and the breakage is only external but not broken through, if it can be recognized easily, it is corbeled within.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the breakage is in the right part (of the jawbone), you must insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; if the breakage is in the left mandible, insert your index finger from the right hand and push gently towards the breakage and align it with the other hand.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jawbone is displaced in two parts, then you must provide two equal extensions until it becomes equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the teeth occurs or breakage, hold them in place with a golden, silver or silk thread, then place a broken mandible splint on it, and put one double cloth on top; and place on the cloth a large well-made stud or equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the mandible, and secure it as you can, and command the patient to rest, and encourage them to eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see the figure change, dislocate it again on the third day, and then reset to its original position; put a plaster over it, made from milled powder with egg or meal of comfrey, after removing the splint; place a light linen plaster over the plaster, and if the plaster swells, remove it, and leave the dislocation until it heals; it often heals in four weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If an abscess comes to the surface, bring what we have said before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, be careful not to remove any piece of the bone with the tools suitable for such.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	If the wound is narrow, enlarge it as needed with fire.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all the pieces and there is no remaining part, close the wound, if it is wide, and apply one or more suitable bandages to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forearm
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks often in front of the shoulder, and the fracture is according to 3 types: either it is broken and dislocated in two places, and it is in several fragments, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedures are when the fracture is with an injury, that you have two assistants, one holds the shoulder where the force is broken; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then align the fracture to your fingers, so that the form should be as it should be, and not have any appearance or protrusion.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, place a round cushion of cloth or linen under the patient's shoulder, and make it as large as necessary; stretch and lift the fracture, and pull the cushion towards your hand, so that you align the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder out by force because it comes in fully, then the patient should lie on his affected side, and place one small pillow under the shoulder; and push the ministers (assistants) downward on the shoulder until the bone of the socket is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then direct the fracture to your fingers, and if you find debris, then it is necessary that you cut above; and draw out the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot join due to any obstruction, strike one of the incisions you have made; but place this instrument under the socket to prevent dislocation.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait .ij. chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os;	and resemble a spoon, not narrow, and be as wide as necessary, according to the size of the bone and the power of the work; and have two prongs, as you see, and one large and the other narrow, like the opening of the wound that you made when treating the bones.
et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And when you are certain of the abscess being hot, if it opens and the wound is small, or you doubt that the abscess is hot, then use linen and bandages on the wound according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if abscesses are cold, moisten a linen cloth in rose oil and asafoetida and wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier;	The binding of the bone, when there are wounds and cuts, is to place a plaster made from flour and egg white on the bone, put light packs on top, and place a splint beneath it if necessary.
puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met .i. drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de .iij. dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant;	Then take a very long bandage of a palm's width, then put one double cloth dampened on top of it, and apply it; then take a thin stick that is three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage, so that the end of the bandage hangs.
et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint;	and place the stick on the fractured bone, and turn the bandage over the neck, and under the patient's armpit, and under the healthy arm; then pull it from each side, and when you see that the splint holds the fracture in alignment, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, keep it in place every day, and when the swelling subsides, hold it.
et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort .i. petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a .xx. jors;	and make the patient lie on his back, and when he sleeps, place a small pillow under his armpit to raise the shoulder; align the fracture by adjusting the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless a bad accident occurs, for up to 20 days.
puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en .xxviij. jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Then resume the treatment, if it seems necessary to you, and hold it and keep it in that state until it is restored; and it is restored in about 28 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	The break of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It often happens that the broken or dislocated shoulder does not heal by itself, and it should only be forced back with the touch; arrange it according to the shape of the dislocation, and reset it in its natural form in all ways possible; then apply powder from the mill with plenty of egg whites, and soft bandages, and put on a double cloth; then put a broad and thin strip, slightly larger than the shoulder, over it, and if there is a hollow under the strip anywhere on the shoulder, fill that hollow with soft bandages of linen, so that the strip lies evenly; and then tighten it firmly, so that the strip does not move from its place, and watch the patient every day; and whenever it swells, tighten it again, and adjust the strip if it is out of its place, and make the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be healed in 20 or 25 days. And when this number is complete, loosen it, and be careful because it is not easy for bone to move lightly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment protrudes in front and not beneath the skin, raise it up, remove it, and do as we have said in the treatment for abscess alleviation by hot cautery.
de la brisure dou pis	of the fracture with a splint
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer. Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	Bone fractures sometimes occur in the middle, but not often; however, they usually break at an angle. And when it is broken inside, it slips downward, causing the patient great pain, and lack of alignment, swelling, and immediately vomiting blood. The openings in the fractured bones appear wide.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down with his face on his back, and one cushion is placed between the shoulders, then the shoulders are pressed and the ribs of the two sides are assembled to your hands, and subtly put it all together in every way that you can, until the shape of the bone is as required; then lay on plasters and poultices of salt or another light substance, wrap it in one bandage, and place it on the broken bone so that it does not move; turn the limb roundabout, stretch it gradually, and every hour check the bandage, and if it becomes soft, tighten it; and if it requires dislocation due to corrosion or inflammation that comes to the place, or pain or abscess, hurry and dislocate it, remove the plaster, and address those who have come in methods of treatment; then reset the plaster, stretch it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rib fracture
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs only comes from large falls on the back and in the chest, and they do not break except when they are slippery; and it is felt well at the investigation with hands.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient. Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And the resetting is that you must set the fracture evenly, as necessary. Then put a splint and bind it with a stick, if needed.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is concave inwards, the patient feels very great pain and shortness of breath, like with pleurisy, because the bone pierces through; and points at the end, and immediately vomits a large quantity of blood, which is a grave illness, and the ancients have made great efforts.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if those who say it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the fracture outwards.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not let hot irons come unless they have come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	If they have come, we heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And someone said that we put leeches on the joint, to draw out pus, which seems reasonable; however, there is doubt whether the leeches will attract the superfluidities to the joint due to its weak composition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And someone said that one should cover the joint with damp linen soaked in hot oil and place a splint between the ribs to make the joint equal on all sides, then it should be cured with the cure of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz .i. estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that does not pierce through the flesh, and doubt exists for the patient, then it is necessary to cut into the rib on the broken side, and a tool should be placed there to support it; and afterwards it must be cut, pulled out gently, and then the two edges of the wound should be sewn together if they are large, and dressed with ointment until it heals. And if an abscess arises, then oil-soaked linen cloths should be placed on it; and treat the rib while it is healing, and let him lie on the affected side until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Occasionally there is a break of the neck bones, and sometimes it bends; and similarly with the spine in the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent. Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	And when this happens to anyone, and you want to know if it will heal or not, take note if you see his hands softened, swollen and dead, and he cannot move or stretch them, and when you prick them with a needle, he does not feel it. Know that he is mortal in many positions, and if he is silent and feels well when they are straightened and pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient will be cured if treatment is applied.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet. Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	And if similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will heal or not, take note if the feet are softened, and if there is injury in the hands, and sudden movement of the wind and evacuation without will; and when it is supported on the stomach, it moves with no will. And when it is supported on its back and wants to sit, it cannot. Know that it is deadly: do not labor in its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this event does not happen to him, it will be an easier situation.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you apply warm oil (either rosin or egg yolk oil) if there is an abscess, then place a comforting and drying ointment on top of it, bind it with a thread, and instruct the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on the part where he feels pain until it heals.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If any bone is dislocated, cover it with oil; remove the bone, then bring together the two edges of the wound, if it is large, by sewing them, and apply a healing ointment made of charred material until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called "the head of the cow", press your left thumb against it and align it with your right hand as far as you can, then place the ointment and dressing on top, if necessary; then tie it, and if there is dislocated bone, push it back, remove it, and heal the wound until it heals.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the break in the shinbone (tibia)
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It happens that the bone of the hip is broken, and if it happens, there is only a little lessening at the head; it extends long and breaks apart at the ends, causing pain to the patient at the place, and pierces and inflames what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, as long as you are above the breakage; and learn which is the breakage and its shape; and if the breakage is only at the head, then equalize the breakage, while it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the breakage is long or it declines inside, then lay the patient on their belly, until the restoration of the breakage comes to you.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.
