And when you have set it even, place the splint upon it, then put a stick or a key on top, and hold the break steady so that it does not move; and keep the limb under the ribs until the break is healed.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	Instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	If an abscess has burst, do not touch it until the abscess has healed, and place what we have previously mentioned on top of it; then return to treatment, hold it as needed, unless there is any bad incident; and this is the manner.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder break
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is that which is between the neck and the upper arm, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of the two ways: one of which is that you take a splint made of large thread, in this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends of the splint with two cords, and raise them upwards, and position the patient supine on one couch; then lay his broken arm on the splint, until it reaches its place, and have a hump of splint in the middle, then raise something heavy above or the assistants stretch it downstream; then place the mirrors the break equal to their hands together, until the break returns as it should.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is to lay the patient on his bed, and tie his hand to his neck, then command two assistants that one holds what is above the break with both hands, and the other holds beneath all the cord, and stretch each side separately.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint .i. liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part. Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes .i. liien moien desoz l’assele, et .i. autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre .i. liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the extraction is forced, hold one ligament beneath the break and one above it, and extend each of the assistants to their part. If the break is near the head of the shoulder, you must put a moderate ligament beneath the dislocation, and another towards the side, beneath the break; and similarly if the break is towards the side, you must put a light one without effort, as long as the break is equal on the joint, and on the side; then make it equal, as required, and hold it, if no abscess comes.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If abscesses come, do not hold it for more than 7 days, and place soft linen with rose oil on top of the abscess to calm it; then you can hold it, and the method of holding is that you put a clamp on the break, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or the chest; and put a cloth on it, and hold it on the shoulder and on the arm so that the arm remains in place, if nothing prevents it, or if the bone is not moving.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you doubt that the bone is moving, use wedges, and place a larger and stronger one on the break than the others, and have at least two inches of space between each wedge, and make each wedge so large that it passes over the break by four inches from each side; then hold them with wedges, as I said at the beginning of the chapter regarding the break, more firmly and less in alignment.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the abscess of the bone and the swelling, as we have said, when you are restoring the broken limb, and doubt the abscess is hot, leave it to heal for up to seven days, as we have said; then look every three days at the healing, that pus does not grow or come to the place, or new swelling comes to the member because it is too tight. Follow this advice, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	If no such accidents happen, do not remove the splint before four days or more; let the patient lie on his back, and keep his hands on his stomach; put a cushion made of equal linen under the shoulder, and look every hour of the day or night to see if the figure of the broken limb moves or if the splint becomes soft; then follow this advice by means of medicine, and give him the meat that was mentioned earlier, in such a way that the meat is initially tender; and when it begins to recover, let it become thick. It is customary that the shoulder and leg should be repositioned within 40 days of the whole accident; then you must remove the splint and administer baths and ointment-like medicines to guide the healing process. If the fracture is crooked and swollen, wait one day or two months to remove it.
de la brisure du bras	on the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "dui" ("two"); one is small, and it is the one that forms the elbow; and the other is large, and it is the one located towards the little finger near the wrist; by accident, only the large bone may break, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When the small bone is broken, restoration and healing are easy; but when the large bone is broken, healing is difficult and more painful than when both are broken together. If it is only the small bone that is broken, you should gently extend it slightly and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	If it is the large bone that is broken, you should apply more force; stretch it up to one inch, raise the elbow of the hand higher than the others, and lower the small finger below the others, and cross the patient's arms over themselves, placing a stick one inch above them to prevent the patient from feeling any labor; then extend the minister's arm to the lower part beneath his hand or to one link, and another minister above. Then make the broken bones even, according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken in pieces, place each piece back in its proper place, and if there is any dislocated part that refuses to return, set the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breakage in wounds, I have spoken about it in a separate chapter; take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if in the beginning of healing, abscesses occur, apply one cloth made of rose oil and white wax that is neither too hard nor too soft; lay one cloth on top of it delicately until the abscess is appeased. Then remove the wax and put in the plaster made from the powder of mill with egg, then insert splints; the splint at the breakage should be more prominent and a bit larger than others; you will need seven splints or more for various positions: whether the breakage is in one bone or two. Keep the splint above the breakage tighter than other places, but looser elsewhere, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are above the breakage be soft and moist, not hard or harsh; and let the threads, which hold it, be of flax, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And observe the member and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad accidents happen to the limb, such as itching that happens to the limb, you should irrigate the limb with warm water until the itching is soothed; and do not let the limb rest. Then begin the binding, and if the ligaments are weakened and the bones dislocated, and similar things, give advice accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the narrowing of the anus cannot reach the limb because it is too narrow, you should soften it a little and leave for some days until the narrowing comes, then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of the things we have mentioned come to the patient, you should not release him until 20 days have passed, or inquire about it within that time. Then lay his hands on his neck and make sure they are even, and keep him from movement and turning, and sleep on his back; know that this fracture will be restored in 30 or 40 days, and possibly in 20 days, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The fracture at the back of the hand and fingers occurs rarely, but it bends repeatedly.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or bent, the patient must cross his arms and sit straight in front of him equally; then he should place his hand on a cloth stretched out, and extend the broken bones, align them with mirrors as they are, until they are well joined; then apply the plaster and bandages, if an abscess does not occur, then place a splint according to the severity of the fracture, and wrap it in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the broken bone is at the groin area around the lower abdomen of the leg, make a splint from cloths, and instruct the patient to bind it to their broken leg; then bind it with a long cloth, and make sure the wooden splint is as thick as the hand, and bind it, as required.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is at the elbow, it is necessary that you place a splint above and another below in the hand, so that the fingers are covered and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and stop the flow between the two bones.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture occurs in any of the fingers, if it is the thumb, make it straight, as required; bind it with the palm, and if you see that it moves, place a small straight splint to hold the fracture steady; and if the fracture is in other fingers like the index or another one, make it straight, and bind it with the adjacent healthy finger; or tie them all together in one bundle, as appropriate, or place a splint on top of it, as with the thumb; take care in the healing and positioning of the abscess, and treat it as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken leg
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the leg are often broken and one sees it when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one tie a splint above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then each minister extends his splint equally to their respective parts; and this is when the break is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	If the break is near the root of the leg, one splint should be towards the heel, and the other splints below the break. And if it is near the knee, then the splints should be on each side of the knee, and the extension should be distal; then adjust the bone equal to its two hands, according to its natural figure, and then apply the plaster and bind, without abscess coming.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that is hot, let it cool down first, then return to your work and your treatment; the process is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should place a bandage made of thick double fabric for two or three layers, and let the excess be removed, then bend the leg so that the heels reach the root of the thigh, and insert one long thread between the calf and the thigh, below the knee joint, and bring the end of the thread to the top; then bend both the leg and the thigh with the bandage, then put the broken bones on either side of the bandage, and place a bone splint over the leg bone; then use soft linen cloth between the leg and the thigh to equalize the binding, then begin to tie four turns or more around the fracture; as you go higher on the fracture, loosen the bindings; then take the two threads that you have inserted between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return to below the top thread, so that you can pass under the foot; tighten it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it, so that there is no sign of an abscess or swelling or anything else.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens (that the broken bone pierces the skin), you should separate them, directing where they are coming from, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that are protruding, they must be cut off, if possible; and if not, the limb must be cut open, and the flesh removed; and treat it as we have said before, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thighbone is broken so that splints are set in it, as in the shoulder and arm; however, when restored in this manner, it does not cause discomfort to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the thighbone is restored within a day, or slightly less or more, according to the variations of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the groin of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the groin of the knee, there is little fracture but it bends often. And if it breaks, it is not a complete break, but rather a fissure or a piercing, causing all pain and pain sensation.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when one equalizes the limb that is dislocated to its joints, as long as it can be assembled; then put the splint on, and place a round piece of iron, if you have need of it, and tighten it as needed; then check all the positions that we have said in other breaks, like an abscess and others; place at each accident whatever is needed, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break in the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called directly "anus" and the other is called "fibula"; and it happens equally as a break in the arm, and therefore the restoration is equal to that of the arm, and the work is all the same.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	If the slender bone is broken, it bends forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	If the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen; it bends underneath. Then apply the extension, make it even, and align the edges equally; however, if the break is misaligned and there are many pieces, the extension should be smaller and lighter; and adjust the alignment according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two fusts that hold the leg from one side and the other, and be as long as the leg from the knee to underneath; then wrap them in two layers, one above and one below, and secure it in the middle so that the leg cannot decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should provide a splint of the length of the leg, and it be made from fust, and place the leg for prevention of movement, and properly make it at the break where there is pain; and move the leg every day, to see if there is abscess or another accident; cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the break of the bones from the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no break, but the bones of the foot sometimes have a break and the toes also, and it does not happen often except in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, place the patient's foot on the ground, as if they were walking, and then place your foot on their foot where the bones are raised, press it until they return to their places; then apply a splint and muffler, and place a small table with two flat cushions under the sole of the foot, then tighten the strap towards the affected foot, after you have wrapped cloths around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when four or six days have passed, undo the strap, because you will find the bones equal, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the two bones are broken, restore them as we have said for the bones of the hand; then set a splint on the broken bone according to the length of the bone, and let it be slightly larger; then place the padding mentioned under the splint and tighten it; and if there are 2 or more, or more, break each bone with a splint, wrapped in one linen cloth, and tighten the padding beneath the splint; and let them remain above the belly of the bone, so that they cover it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other breaks, after we have said them; and treat each injury as necessary.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the finger bone break
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of the female pelvis is broken, make her sit with legs spread apart, then incline her to the part of the back and hold her from behind; fill the cavity with cotton and put as much as a stone in it; then turn the woman, lift up the buttocks little by little, and when the cotton reaches the entrance of the pelvis, the bone will return with the stone; when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, replace it, and do this for seven days or more: the fracture will be restored. If you see, take a bladder of barley, and tie one end of a string to it, and push the entire bladder into the pelvis; then inflate the string forcefully until the bladder is swollen inside: the fracture will return; fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the wrist of a man or woman is broken, restore it in the same way as we have said regarding the bone of the thigh; and these fractures should not be hidden from him who applies his study and use to them, and pay attention to my book. For fractures signify in many ways the right way of restoration: therefore, take note of this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis (verge), when it is broken, take a goose's throat and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for three days or more, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	With break (or fracture) with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	For the one who has a break (or fracture) with wound, especially if it is large such as the bone of the leg or shoulder or similar, it should be cleaned now, as the cleansings that we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, anoint it with vinegar (or other solution), then proceed to restore the break in that same hour or on that day, unless abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If abscesses appear, wait until the ninth day for restoration, allowing the abscess to calm down, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, because you would bring about a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and appears under the skin, it should be set gently with light pressure and small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the fractured bone cannot be set equal to your hands, it should be set with this tool which is of iron, about 7 or 8 inches long, and the width according to the size of the wound; therefore, it is necessary for the mirror that he takes 3 or 4 depending on what is needed in each treatment of fracture; it should be round and slightly large, so it does not bend during the setting process of the member in your work, and it should be sharp at the tip and thick from the middle forward.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche", because the curved shoulders should be placed on top of the apparent bone; and push it once, until it returns, and let it be even one against the other. If the fracture is subtle and the instruments cannot well take hold of the bone, then you must cut the head of the bone, so that the instruments have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, if you have an appropriate instrument such as a chisel or saw, at your power; then strike that part of the bone which remains in the bone with sharpness and small chips.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone has been brought back and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place. You must continue to set it until it is in its proper position, then moisten a linen cloth in black-stiptic vinegar, and make sure it is not hot; do not apply it over the seared wound or anything that has oil, as it may cause decay and corruption; instead, administer stitches when you have restored the bone, leaving the wound exposed, and cover the surrounding area according to the size of the wound, taking care not to compress the wound with the fracture; and many times this has been done by the foolish surgeon, causing death or rotting of the patient sometimes; let the ligatures be softer and more flexible than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that evil accident may come, as we have said, and you find pain at the place, do not put poultices on it; instead wrap around it, in place of poultices, hard cloths and bind it.  And when after one day or two, you see new fluid coming from the wound, remove whatever you had applied and apply healing ointment to the wound, such as therapeutic ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	You should loosen the limb two times a day, in the morning and at evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	The limbs should be arranged in such a way that the bone moves downwards gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it remains for many days and cannot heal but continues to boil, know that there are small bone fragments, which is why you must be careful with the wound and remove all the loose fragments that cause the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If a fistula or some other form of corruption appears, you must treat it, as stated in the chapter before this one. And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and similar large limbs, do not drain it, because many times death occurs, but let it heal by itself; perhaps it will close up after twenty or thirty days. Then treat the wound if you can; if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	broken bones that come upon a suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often encounter [the condition] after health following the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a disfigured sight to see the form of the limb; and unfortunately, the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore, take care of the fracture: administer medicines such as aloes, incense, myrrh, saracolle, acacia, and similar others, taking any one of these things or all together, and grind them with a stifling wine or with a lot of egg white or ashes; and put it on the knot in bandages, and tighten it well, and do not loosen it for many days; and then dislocate it, and start another, until the swelling is removed; or you hold above a piece of plank well made; for the properties of the plank are such that it removes all inflammations from the limbs; and if the nodulation has turned into hardness like stone, it must be removed, if the head is exposed, and make the excess apparent; or you shave it with any rasp, until it is removed, and cure it when it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb that is weak after treatment
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is set and remains afterwards, the limbs are weak and delicate, this happens for various reasons: one reason being that it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or due to an abundance of swelling; or because of excessive movements, not within its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and to make his body lean, until the blood is multiplied in him; then provide baths, and give joy and sweetness; afterwards apply ointment on the member, so that the ointment attracts great nourishment, and reduce the swelling often with cold water, until the nourishment goes to the member; and return it to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When members are twisted after restoration and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that a member must be broken anew, and many fools have done this in our land; this practice is condemned, and it brings great harm, and perhaps death. However, if the nodulations and tortures are fresh, it is necessary that they should be softened with hot water or with softening herbs such as violet leaves, roots, medicks, and similar things; and you make a soothing poultice, like daqquilon well made. You also take the musk of violets, and mix it with ginger oil or linseed oil, and apply the poultice on it. Or you take figs oiled, grind them with colon flour, and similar medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And sometimes the node is cut off by rubbing continuously and for a long time with moist hands. Movement should be brought to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortures are old and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to cut it with iron, it should be covered up to the bone, at the incision made gently with a sharp instrument; and put cushions and soft fabrics in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in anyone, now it must be returned with care.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one waits, the joint swells, and in case it is put back to its place with force; therefore, one should not move it until the swelling has subsided, for many times it causes pus and other pain.
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	Whenever this happens, clean the patient, then let him rest until all abscesses have subsided; then immerse the affected limb in hot water and oil, gently massage it, and treat each member as medicine requires at its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations of the head from the neck to the feet.
des mandibules	of the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	1. It often happens that the lower jaws are dislocated, and the dislocations of both sides are in two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their place and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the lower part, and the saliva drops out of the mouth that it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is slight, it returns in more ways.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it is complete and accomplished, you must reset it promptly, without delay;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a manner that the minister grasps the head of the patient, and presses one of his fingers from one hand into the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other hand should be opened, to make them even; and instructs the patient to soften, their jaws, and move them from all sides.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the fingers are equalized, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, then immerse them in hot water and oil, until they are gently reset, do not force it, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they (the dislocated limbs) are reset equally, the mouth of the patient should be closed and softened with a cloth soaked in an ointment made of rose oil and wax, then it should be tied gently with several bands.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	and the patient should sleep on his back with his shoulders between two pillows, so that he does not move to either side nor tries to exert himself in any way, but should take light food until the pains have subsided, and the jaws should be tied.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	and then he should eat lightly whatever he wants, but he must not exert himself in opening his mouth for eating or drinking, until the jaws are well tied and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jawbones cannot be set right within an hour and are not converted to their proper place, fevers and accustomed sweating come, and possibly rupture of the stomach, and possibly vomiting clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is ruin; and many times he who experiences this dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the noose   (specifically a noose used in executions)
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The splint cannot dislocate within the ribcage and along the spine, and it is dislocated once to the side, and this is felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies supine on his back and extends his arms; then presses the joint forward with your palm, and it will return; then put the splint and bind it, and hold it tightly.
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	and the joint that is towards the costal cannot dislocate; if it does not, but if it dislocates once, then reset it to its place as we have said; then put the splint and bind it, and hold it tightly, and instruct the patient to rest until he recovers.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And likewise, the head of the spine is reset when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	When the shoulder joint is dislocated.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated in only four ways: The first way is when it dislocates to the lower part of the socket; and the second is at the back part; and occasionally it dislocates at the upper part, but this rarely happens;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	It does not dislocate behind the shoulder or inside the nerves, and it often dislocates downward towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, because it can easily move out of place; for those with enough flesh, it moves out only slightly, and returns quickly.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes happens to some men, percussion or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you should verify [the shoulder], until you are sure; and then start the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	Dislocation is known when it moves towards the joint and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one. You will find a clear distinction between them.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find a hollow at the top of the shoulder, and below press on the lower part of the shoulder as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot return his hand to its place nor move in any way.
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And if it is dislocated upwards, do not hide this, for you will clearly feel it by pressing.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	This method of dislocation is not only to be returned when it is new, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the patient's hand up high, then places his thumbs underneath the joint, and forces the joint upward to its place; the minister lifts the hand, and stretches it up, puts it back down; it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	If it does not come as we have said in hand days after, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and bring comforting and soothing ointment, such as a decotion of althea and fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and bring this.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then the patient should be placed on his back, and put a piece of linen equal to the joint under the heel, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the minister's foot on the cloth, and pull the head of the shoulder upwards properly, and draw the patient's hand.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another servant binds the patient's head so that it does not move downward; the shoulder immediately returns to its place, and if you see this happening, reset it in this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	and place a person larger than the patient on the opposite side of the shoulder, facing towards its costal region, and press the patient's shoulder down, lifting their head so that the patient hangs over the edge;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another servant pulls the patient's hand downward towards their abdomen. If the patient is too light, give them something heavy to hold, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And it is also reset in another way: and this is when a long needle is inserted into the earth, with the head being as round as a pea, and not too thick nor too thin;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	then it is placed beneath the patient, but with a soft cloth on top, and the patient should be lying down longwise along the staff; then his hand should be extended on the other side and the joint will return to its place quickly;
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	and if it does not return due to all the things we have said, then perform this cure: take a needle that is two arms long and four fingers wide, which has a round head for entering deeply into the assele (shoulder socket) in this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay the rod, wrapped in cloth, on top of the patient's head, so that it does not prick the patient, then place him under the cushion of the patient; extend his arm above the long rod, and tie the shoulder to the rod, and the forearm at the end of the upper arm, then lift the arm onto one iron hook of a scale with a large hole, and spread out the hands below, and leave the body hanging from the other side: the joint will be relocated in this manner.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, whichever way that may be, you must put an equal piece of wool under the cushion, then apply the plaster made of mill powder, along with incense and egg whites, over the entire shoulder and around, then tie it under the cushion with a thread, turn the thread around the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and keep the hands in this manner.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary to give food, as long as the limbs are comfortable, because it will heal faster; and then give more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it becomes hard and does not soften, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is dislocated due to moisture that has come, or for another reason, then you must administer three fire cauteries as stated in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	If you do all of this and it still dislocates again after 7 days, and the joint cannot hold and cannot lift its arm above, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is either cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint can never be pushed back into place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the thighs or hips, and the backside, is caused by forceful pushing and stretching with hands, and another method of treatment is applied; and it is cured when it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the healing comes swelling to the member, and it moves slowly; have the patient use baths many times until the swelling subsides, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	Of the dislocation, the cost is great.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the jointure of cost is dislocated at points, and at points it returns; and if it is dislocated in all parts, both front and back, and the dislocation is not repaired, for it can be seen well and felt well; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement. Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	And when you join the sick person's shoulder with the healthy one, make sure you can see it clearly. For the joint is dislocated and cannot bend the arm or touch the shoulder completely.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	Then you must reset the dislocation as soon as an abscess opens up, for if an abscess opens up, it is harmful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and in many cases death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is when it can be reset that you extend your hand to its two hands; and his arms should be spread out, and the hands of the mirror according to the shoulder around it, above and below, and push the joint back to its sockets together, or to the root of the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is at the front, it returns when it doubles its hand to its hand, and pierces the root of the palm that has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and they bind it with two ministers, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm on each side, then when you have wound a double-length and wide cloth around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	and when the master joins the joint to the hand, he applies some oil to soften the joint, then presses the joint firmly until it returns.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And when it is in place, place dry plaster made with egg white on it and hold it firmly, and have the patient keep his arm at his neck, and leave it for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firmly held in place, remove the bandage and leave it alone; if you see that the joint does not hold properly, repeat the plaster and bandage, and leave it like this for some days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	If it feels grating after the reset of the joint and it swells, bathe it well and scrub it, and press until it is soothed; or put a lamb's wool pad on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and let it enter the water.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when it swells, gently rub the joint, then place the nail on top, and then immerse [the affected area]; and do this 2 or 3 times until it is healed; and if you see, place warm moistened hay wrapped in butter on it and hold it; it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	swelling of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is quick to dislocate more than other joints; it must be returned to its place quickly as soon as it is dislocated, unless the lews are swollen or there is hot abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne.	And the re-positioning is that you place the sick hand on a table, and extend the minister's hand, and make the damaged part equal, so that it places its palm over the appearance of the jointure, and push until it returns.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Furthermore, you should look if it is in its proper position; then place the patient's hand palm down on a table for both extension and repositioning.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele aparance de la jointure. S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, place the patient's hand palm down on the table, and make your hand over the appearance of the jointure. If it returns now, that is good.
Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, hold a warm poultice against abscesses that have been opened, and leave it to start healing.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if it cannot bear weight, and you are unable to set it again within certain days, then the dislocated joint remains unhealed.
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and it does not help the patient unless his hand is numb, and he cannot exert any pressure: know then that the nerves are cut or the arteries; there is no other remedy but to compress with a fire cautery in this case, and perhaps nothing else works.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put the poultice we have mentioned on it, then compress and leave it for 5 days, then release and let it be as it is.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no grating, moist warm water, and rub it until it becomes clean.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	Of the dislocations of the fingers of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre;	The fingers of the hand are sometimes dislocated on both sides, sometimes at the back of the palm or belly.
adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins;	Then push the finger, and apply the dislocation to your chest as it returns, then hold the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated.
et le laisse .ij. jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit,	And let it rest for two days, then equalize it on that day; and bind it, as we have said, and release it from binding, and make it move, and rebind it; and do this frequently, until it is tight.
et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	And do the same if it is dislocated from the abdomen of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and do the same when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the vertebra in the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the vertebra in the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, as death quickly approaches the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les .ij. cuixes ou li dui bras ou .j.	And the signs are that the stools pass without control and cannot be held, and many limbs become softened, such as the two legs or the two arms or one.
Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a iiij. pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»:	And many times the vertebra in the lower back becomes paralyzed, and it is called "gibbosity."
li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	The physician should note whether the ailment is due to childhood gynecological problems, as there will be no cure or healing in that case.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit;	And those resulting from falling or blows or similar things, the old methods of healing have spoken of in great words, but they are not always beneficial.
mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	I have abridged it according to my intention and made instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit;	I say that in the gynecological problem mentioned earlier, there is no remedy or healing.
et ausi cele que vient droitement en .ij. costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis;	And similarly the one that comes straight into two sides, can be cured by no other than the one who comes from behind, as I said;
et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en .i. leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece;	and the patient should be extended on his back in one even place, and have someone hold him under to prevent bleeding;
puis fiche .i. tison au chief en terre forment, et .i. autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et .i. autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles;	then insert one needle in the head into the earth, and another at the feet, and tie a rope around the ankles of the patient, and another around the knees, hips, and ankles;
et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les .ij. tisons;	And two ministers know the ligaments, one to the head and others to the feet, among the four tendons;
et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	And let them be well closed, the tendons as we have said, and the mirrors place their hands on the spine, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de .iij. bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee;	And if it does not return by this cure, take a board four spans long and sharpened at the end, and place the patient on his side, then push the top of the board under the side, then put the middle of the board on the spine;
et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	and place the mirrors feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do it with the turning wheel that rotates by hand.  (This is referring to the use of a device called a traction splint or "tornet" to reposition dislocated bones.)
Et est que tu fiches .ij. tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez .ij. autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc;	And you stick two needles in the head of the patient's arm of great length, and between each needle, an inch of space from one another;
et ait en chescun tison .i. pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns .ij. tisons ait .i. tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en .ij. tornans .ij. petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet;	and have one prick for each needle where the tendon turns, and let the needles be firmly in the earth so they do not move; and between two needles have one turning needle, like a rope, and have two small needles of an inch long for turning the turning needle to turn the tendon.
et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	and then tie the cord that is among the tendons to the tendon towards the head, and the other cord towards the feet at the other tendon, and each minister turns his tendon all along the cord, and the master puts the splint equal as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de .iij. dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez;	And when it is even, place a drying plaster on it with much egg, then pound it, then the stick of a table-flat three fingers long, which brings out the swelling and the healthy part of the spine, then tie it with a string, as we have said, and use the patient with gentle nursing, until it is healed;
et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc,	and if anything comes at the end of healing, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines with the stick we have mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered.
et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And sometimes the appearance comes at the lower part of the spine, and it is thought to be a dislocation; but this is the bone that opens, for which reason one should not have presumption, because in such a case death may come.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of the dislocations of the shoulder
