Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Note that the dislocations of the shoulder and the shoulder joint occur only due to dislocations and not like other joints; and the shoulder joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more on the inside, and less so in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer and more open the sick person's knee than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee in the fire;
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	and it is the loosened area that is swollen with abscess, because the calf of the leg comes there.   | The text means that when a dislocation occurs in the shoulder joint, it causes the limb to be misaligned, causing pain and injury to the patient. Additionally, the shoulder joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more on the inside, and less so in front and back. The knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the sick leg with the healthy one, it is longer and more open the sick person's knee than the healthy one, and the sick person cannot bend their knee in the fire. The swelling of the area with abscess occurs because the calf of the leg comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that whose it comes to dislocation, is that this event is opposite to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that whose it happens before, are that his leg is well set according to the completion; however, do not double the knee pain, and if you wish to make him walk, he cannot move forward, and he retains his urine, and swells the ankle, and when he goes, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that whose it happens after, are that he cannot extend his knee, nor double it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is in the place beneath the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The re-alignments of this kind of dislocation are such that you observe whether the dislocations are old and remain according to their position without any treatment; and it is not necessary that there should be any assumption made about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	In the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four kinds of dislocations, you hurry up to turn the joint, and push it inwards and outwards, and move it left and right; by chance if it returns, no further treatment is required.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles .i. ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a .ij. mains, ou a .i. liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil;	If it does not return in this manner, then you must prepare one strong assistant and hold the leg firmly with two hands or with one link attached above the knee.
et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien;	and another minister extends his hand over in such a manner that he pushes his hands under the knees, then tightens a rope-like loop on the thigh; and another grips the head of the loop;
et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	and they all extend up and down at once, until the patient is lifted from the ground once, and hangs there.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common for the four similar cases, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance. Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele;	If not (the shoulder), it is necessary to treat its appearance. When the dislocation is at the front, it is necessary that you raise the patient on their sound side, then place the rope around the root of the thigh, and the part that is under the angle, then tighten the rope towards the angle, and towards the neck;
puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	Then take another assistant and grasp the large part of the diseased thigh, and extend it outwards in the form of a bow; if it returns to its place now; and this method of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les .ij. piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les .ij. talons, et sus les .ij. genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue .ij. dois plus que li autres;	And if you cannot hold it in this manner as we have said, then tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong cord above the heels and knees, and let the diseased leg be extended two feet more than the others;
puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre .ij. bras de lonc; puis comande a .j. ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Then let him be hanged by the neck from a post, and his legs should be .j. (two) arms' length above the ground; then command one minister to embrace the thigh, and another minister should be hanging with the patient, who should then embrace the thigh, for the joint is returning now quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne .i. liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi;	And when dislocation occurs at the hip, let the patient lie as we have said in the one who has slipped, and draw a cord around the affected leg properly, and also around the pelvis.
puis met .ij. tisons, .i. au chief et .i. autre as piez, puis fiche .i. tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme;	Then insert two needles, one at the neck and one at the feet, then pass a needle between the thighs at the patient's groin.
et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And it should be planted with moist cloths around, so as not to burn the patient, then each minister should extend towards him, and the mirror place equal distance from its hand to the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin. Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If it returns, that's good. If not, put it on a table and press as we have said in the swelling, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it should be extended immediately, as I have said; and place the mirror on the opposite side of the diseased angle, then press with the other hand, and draw it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is toward the outside, it should not be stretched out further nor raised above the ground, but rather it should remain as when a bed is dislocated to the outside, as we have said in the lying down on two beds;
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and it should be on its face, and the limb stretched out as we have said before, and press upon the joint against the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and will be in place when the patient extends his legs, and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and put the splint, and tie it with a bandage so that the bed does not move;
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And it rests for three or four days, then you dislocate it, and place a splint on it; if they are even, hold them steady as before, and let it be. Three days; then you dislocate it again, and make it walk well, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: inside, outside, and backside; do not dislocate it forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and if it does not bend at the knee, know that it is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	and the restoration of all [parts] is that you make the patient sit straight, extend their leg if they can, place your back on their chest, and put their foot on your feet.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	then take hold of their thighs with your hands, pull them apart between your palms, then bend the two sides of the thighs together; and another servant extends their foot so that the thigh returns to its place, and the signs are that it bends lightly at the knee.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And place the plaster on top, and make the leg straight from the knee to the ankle, and let them remain together strongly for 3 or 4 days, then release it; and do not let the patient walk until the limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb is not straight, administer strong stretching, as we have said in the treatment of the hernia, until it heals.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the ankle dislocation
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes smashed, and sometimes completely dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it tends towards the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The re-alignment is light, and it should be stretched lightly with the hands when it is only smashed.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated completely, you must make the patient sit upright, and tie four ministers around the leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then to your left hand twice, then raise it up and push the foot strongly upward;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this twice as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, repeat the process, for it will return;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return in this way, make the patient lie down on his back on the ground, and make a firm passageway with a stick between his legs, and tie rags around it so that it does not hurt the patient;
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then mark the ministers the thigh, and another minister extends the foot to his hands or at least one joint, so that he lies across the neck of the foot.
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then each minister extends equally, and the assistants should be close between the patient's thighs to hold the patient when he is stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then the mirrors equalize the dislocation in their hands, and another minister marks the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is set, place the plaster and padding on top, form it, bind the leg to the foot, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle, so the ligatures are not too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Leave it for 2 or 3 days, and if the ligaments loosen, tighten them again; then release it on the third day or the fourth, and keep the patient in bed for four days.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	If it goes beyond that time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess comes to the surface, you must drain it, as we have said before, until it is healed.
des dois	The two [hands]
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two hands are dislocated, they must be carefully extended without exertion, and it is an easy thing to do.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is at any angle in relation to the back or feet, then you must make the patient sit on a flat surface (or table) straight up and place your foot over the affected joints, then press firmly on your foot until it returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it is level and nothing appears, place a table with two legs under the foot of the patient, then apply force, leave it for three days, then release it; let it rest until it heals.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	About wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When a wound comes with dislocation, and it needs to be restored, many times the patient dies:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not presumptuous in healing, if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate, merciful, and slow, do not be brave.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	And at the beginning, use cooling abscesses, and leave the patient in the hands of God, if you see no hope of health.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	and when you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, as soon as the abscess subsides.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is in place, administer soothing things to abscess heat and heal the wound, as needed, with cauterized ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	If there is a dislocation with broken bones and small splinters, set the bone, and do what we have said for simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And beware of entering into fear, as I have said, because it is useful to you according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your weapon and body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	The end of the medical textbook.
